style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">\xe2\x80\xa2&#160;<span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Estonian_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Estonian Declaration of Independence">Independence declared</a></span> </div></th><td>\n<span class="nowrap">24 February 1918</span></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div (Russian\xe2\x80\x93Estonian)">Treaty of Tartu (Russian-Estonian)<br />with independence recognized</a></span> </div></th><td>\n2 February 1920</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div Estonia">+372</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:EE" title="ISO 3166-2:EE">EE</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/.ee" title=".ee">.ee</a><sup>e</sup></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">\n<li value="2">According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Estonia" title="Constitution of Estonia">Constitution of Estonia</a>, Estonian is the sole official language.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/V%C3%B5rumaa" class="mw-redirect" title="V\xc3\xb5rumaa">southern counties</a>, <a href="/wiki/V%C3%B5ro_language" title="V\xc3\xb5ro language">V\xc3\xb5ro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seto_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Seto language">Seto</a> are spoken along with it. <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> is spoken in parts of <a href="/wiki/Ida-Virumaa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ida-Virumaa">Ida-Virumaa</a> and Tallinn.</li><li value="3">Including 5.4% <a href="/wiki/V%C3%B5ros" title="V\xc3\xb5ros">V\xc3\xb5ros</a> and 0.93% <a href="/wiki/Setos" title="Setos">Setos</a>.<span style="font-size: 120%;"><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></span></li><li value="4">47,549&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (18,359&#160;sq&#160;mi) were defined according to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tartu_(Russian%E2%80%93Estonian)" title="Treaty of Tartu (Russian\xe2\x80\x93Estonian)">Treaty of Tartu</a> in 1920 between Estonia and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet Russia">Soviet Russia</a> (then <a href="/wiki/Communist" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist">communist</a> <a href="/wiki/Bolshevik" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik">Bolshevik</a> revolutionary government before 1923 organization of USSR). Today, the remaining 2,323&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (897&#160;sq&#160;mi) are part of <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>/<a href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a>. The ceded areas include most of the former <a href="/wiki/Petseri_County" title="Petseri County">Petseri County</a> and areas behind the <a href="/wiki/Narva_river" class="mw-redirect" title="Narva river">Narva river</a> including <a href="/wiki/Ivangorod" title="Ivangorod">Ivangorod</a> (Jaanilinn).<span style="font-size: 120%;"><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></span> <a href="/wiki/Pechory" title="Pechory">Pechory</a> remains under Russian administration.</li><li value="5">Also <a href="/wiki/.eu" title=".eu">.eu</a>, shared with other member states of the European Union.</li>\n</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Estonia</b> (<a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a>: <i lang="et">Eesti</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Estonian_and_Finnish" title="Help:IPA/Estonian and Finnish">[\xcb\x88e\xcb\x90sti]</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Et-Eesti.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5e/Et-Eesti.ogg" class="internal" title="Et-Eesti.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>), officially the <b>Republic of Estonia</b> (Estonian: <i lang="et">Eesti Vabariik</i><span style="margin-left:1px">)</span>, is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Europe" title="Northern Europe">Northern Europe</a>. It is bordered to the north by the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Finland" title="Gulf of Finland">Gulf of Finland</a> with <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> on the other side, to the west by the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> with <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> to the west (<a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a> to the far west and north), to the south by <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a> (343&#160;km), and to the east by <a href="/wiki/Lake_Peipus" title="Lake Peipus">Lake Peipus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> (338.6&#160;km).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The territory of Estonia consists of a mainland and 2,222 islands in the Baltic Sea,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> covering a total area of 45,227&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (17,462&#160;sq&#160;mi), water 2,839&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (1,096&#160;sq&#160;mi), land area 42,388&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (16,366&#160;sq&#160;mi), and is influenced by a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a>. The official language of the country, <a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a>, is the second most spoken <a href="/wiki/Finnic_languages" title="Finnic languages">Finnic language</a>.\n</p><p>The territory of Estonia has been inhabited since at least 9,000 B.C. <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Estonia" title="Ancient Estonia">Ancient Estonians</a> were some of the last European pagans to be <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianized</a>, following the <a href="/wiki/Livonian_Crusade" title="Livonian Crusade">Livonian Crusade</a> in the <a href="/wiki/13th_century" title="13th century">13th century</a>. After centuries of successive rule by <a href="/wiki/Teutonic_Order" title="Teutonic Order">Germans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Danes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Swedes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Livonia" title="Duchy of Livonia">Poles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Estonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Estonia">Russians</a>, a distinct <a href="/wiki/Estonian_national_awakening" title="Estonian national awakening">Estonian national identity</a> began to emerge the <a href="/wiki/19th_century" title="19th century">19th</a> and early <a href="/wiki/20th_century" title="20th century">20th centuries</a>. This culminated in <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tartu_(Russian%E2%80%93Estonian)" title="Treaty of Tartu (Russian\xe2\x80\x93Estonian)">independence from the Russian Empire</a> in 1918 after a brief <a href="/wiki/Estonian_War_of_Independence" title="Estonian War of Independence">War of Independence</a> at the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. Initially democratic, Estonia was governed by authoritarian rule<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> since 1934 during the <a href="/wiki/Era_of_Silence" title="Era of Silence">Era of Silence</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> (1939-1945), Estonia was <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Baltic_states" title="Occupation of the Baltic states">repeatedly contested and occupied</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>, ultimately being incorporated into the former as the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Estonian Soviet Socialist Republic">Estonian Soviet Socialist Republic</a>. After the loss of its <i>de facto</i> independence, Estonia\'s <a href="/wiki/State_continuity_of_the_Baltic_states" title="State continuity of the Baltic states"><i>de jure</i> state continuity</a> was preserved by the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_government-in-exile" title="Estonian government-in-exile">Estonian government-in-exile</a>, which was recognized by much of the Western World throughout the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> (1945-1991). In 1987 the peaceful <a href="/wiki/Singing_Revolution" title="Singing Revolution">Singing Revolution</a> began against Soviet rule, resulting in the restoration of <i>de facto</i> independence on <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d&#39;\xc3\xa9tat attempt">20 August 1991</a>.\n</p><p>Since independence, Estonia has been a democratic <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a> divided into fifteen <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Estonia" title="Counties of Estonia">counties</a>. Its capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">Tallinn</a>. With a population of 1.3&#160;million, it is one of the least-populous member states of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> since joining in 2004, the economic monetary <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, and of the Western military alliance of the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">North Atlantic Treaty Organization</a> (NATO). It is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a> with an advanced, <a href="/wiki/High-income_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="High-income economy">high-income economy</a> that has been among the fastest-growing in the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Estonia ranks very high in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-HDI_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDI-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and performs favourably in measurements of <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">economic freedom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World_(report)" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom in the World (report)">civil liberties</a>, education,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">press freedom</a> (third in the world in 2012 and 2007).<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Estonian citizens are provided with <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Free_education" title="Free education">free education</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and the longest-paid <a href="/wiki/Maternity_leave" class="mw-redirect" title="Maternity leave">maternity leave</a> in the OECD.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> One of the world\'s most digitally advanced societies,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> in 2005 Estonia became the first state to hold elections over the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_voting_in_Estonia" title="Electronic voting in Estonia">Internet</a>, and in 2014 the first state to provide <a href="/wiki/E-residency_of_Estonia" class="mw-redirect" title="E-residency of Estonia">e-residency</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span href="#Middle_Ages"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Middle Ages</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Swedish_Era"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Swedish Era</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#Russian_Era_and_National_Awakening"><span class="tocnumber">2.4</span> <span class="toctext">Russian Era and National Awakening</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#Independence"><span class="tocnumber">2.5</span> <span class="toctext">Independence</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Second_World_War"><span class="tocnumber">2.6</span> <span class="toctext">Second World War</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Soviet_Period"><span class="tocnumber">2.7</span> <span class="toctext">Soviet Period</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Restoration_of_Independence"><span class="tocnumber">2.8</span> <span class="toctext">Restoration of Independence</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Territorial_history_timeline"><span class="tocnumber">2.9</span> <span class="toctext">Territorial history timeline</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Geography"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Geography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Biodiversity"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Biodiversity</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Politics"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Politics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Parliament"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Parliament</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Government"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Government</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Law"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Law</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Administrative_divisions"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">Administrative divisions</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Foreign_relations"><span class="tocnumber">4.5</span> <span class="toctext">Foreign relations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Military"><span class="tocnumber">4.6</span> <span class="toctext">Military</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Economic_indicators"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Economic indicators</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Historic_development"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Historic development</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Resources"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Resources</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Industry_and_environment"><span class="tocnumber">5.4</span> <span class="toctext">Industry and environment</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Trade"><span class="tocnumber">5.5</span> <span class="toctext">Trade</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Society"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Society</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Urbanization"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Urbanization</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Religion"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Languages"><span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext">Languages</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Education_and_science"><span class="tocnumber">6.5</span> <span class="toctext">Education and science</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Music"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Music</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Literature"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Literature</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Media"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Media</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#Architecture"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Architecture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Holidays"><span class="tocnumber">7.5</span> <span class="toctext">Holidays</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-39"><a href="#Cuisine"><span class="tocnumber">7.6</span> <span class="toctext">Cuisine</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">7.7</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41"><a href="#International_rankings"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">International rankings</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-47"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian language</a>, the oldest known <a href="/wiki/Endonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Endonym">endonym</a> of the Estonians was <i lang="et" title="Estonian language text">maarahvas</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-ariste_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ariste-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> meaning "country people" or "people of the soil". The land inhabited by Estonians was called <i>Maavald</i> meaning "Country Realm" or "Land Realm".\n</p><p>One hypothesis regarding the modern name of Estonia is that it originated from the <i><a href="/wiki/Aesti" title="Aesti">Aesti</a></i>, a people described by the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> historian <a href="/wiki/Tacitus" title="Tacitus">Tacitus</a> in his <i><a href="/wiki/Germania_(book)" title="Germania (book)">Germania</a></i> (ca. 98&#160;AD).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The historic <i>Aesti</i> were allegedly <a href="/wiki/Balts" title="Balts">Baltic people</a>, whereas the modern Estonians are <a href="/wiki/Finno-Ugric_peoples" title="Finno-Ugric peoples">Finno-Ugric</a>. The geographical areas between Aesti and Estonia do not match, with Aesti being farther south.\n</p><p>Ancient Scandinavian <a href="/wiki/Sagas" class="mw-redirect" title="Sagas">sagas</a> refer to a land called <i>Eistland</i>, as the country is still called in <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">Icelandic</a>, and close to the Danish, German, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">Norwegian</a> term <i>Estland</i> for the country. Early <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> and other ancient versions of the name are <i>Estia</i> and <i>Hestia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>Esthonia</i> was a common alternative English spelling before 1921;<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> the country was admitted to the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> under this name, and it continued in the international organization\'s records until December 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Estonia" title="History of Estonia">History of Estonia</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory_and_Viking_Age">Prehistory and Viking Age</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory and Viking Age">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Estonia" title="Ancient Estonia">Ancient Estonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oeselians" title="Oeselians">Oeselians</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kalmev%C3%A4li_.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Kalmev%C3%A4li_.jpg/220px-Kalmev%C3%A4li_.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Kalmev%C3%A4li_.jpg/330px-Kalmev%C3%A4li_.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Kalmev%C3%A4li_.jpg/440px-Kalmev%C3%A4li_.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kalmev%C3%A4li_.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> stone-cist graves</div></div></div>\n<p>Human settlement in Estonia became possible 13,000 to 11,000&#160;years ago, when the ice from the last <a href="/wiki/Ice_age" title="Ice age">glacial era</a> melted. The oldest known settlement in Estonia is the <a href="/wiki/Pulli_settlement" title="Pulli settlement">Pulli settlement</a>, which was on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A4rnu_River" class="mw-redirect" title="P\xc3\xa4rnu River">river P\xc3\xa4rnu</a>, near the town of <a href="/wiki/Sindi,_Estonia" title="Sindi, Estonia">Sindi</a>, in south-western Estonia. According to <a href="/wiki/Radiocarbon_dating" title="Radiocarbon dating">radiocarbon dating</a> it was settled around 11,000&#160;years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-Laurisaar_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Laurisaar-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The earliest human inhabitation during the <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> period is connected to the <a href="/wiki/Kunda_culture" title="Kunda culture">Kunda culture</a>, named after the town of <a href="/wiki/Kunda,_Estonia" title="Kunda, Estonia">Kunda</a> in northern Estonia. At that time the country was covered with forests, and people lived in semi-nomadic communities near bodies of water. Subsistence activities consisted of hunting, gathering and fishing.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Around 4900 BC appear ceramics of the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">neolithic</a> period, known as <a href="/wiki/Narva_culture" title="Narva culture">Narva culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Starting from around 3200 BC the <a href="/wiki/Corded_Ware_culture" title="Corded Ware culture">Corded Ware culture</a> appeared; this included new activities like primitive agriculture and animal husbandry.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> started around 1800 BC, and saw the establishment of the first <a href="/wiki/Hillfort" title="Hillfort">hill fort</a> settlements.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> A transition from hunting-fishing-gathering subsistence to single-farm-based settlement started around 1000 BC, and was complete by the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> around 500 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-Laurisaar_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Laurisaar-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The large amount of bronze objects indicate the existence of active communication with Scandinavian and Germanic tribes.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KumnaHoardArtfs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/KumnaHoardArtfs.jpg/220px-KumnaHoardArtfs.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/KumnaHoardArtfs.jpg/330px-KumnaHoardArtfs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/KumnaHoardArtfs.jpg/440px-KumnaHoardArtfs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KumnaHoardArtfs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> artefacts of a hoard from <a href="/wiki/Kumna" title="Kumna">Kumna</a><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>A more troubled and war-ridden middle Iron Age followed, with external threats appearing from different directions. Several Scandinavian <a href="/wiki/Sagas" class="mw-redirect" title="Sagas">sagas</a> referred to major confrontations with Estonians, notably when Estonians defeated and killed the Swedish king <a href="/wiki/Ingvar" title="Ingvar">Ingvar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Similar threats appeared in the east, where Russian principalities were expanding westward. In 1030 <a href="/wiki/Yaroslav_the_Wise" title="Yaroslav the Wise">Yaroslav the Wise</a> defeated Estonians and established a fort in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Tartu" title="Tartu">Tartu</a>; this foothold lasted until an Estonian tribe, the Sosols, destroyed it in 1061, followed by their raid on <a href="/wiki/Pskov" title="Pskov">Pskov</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Around the 11th century, the Scandinavian Viking era around the Baltic Sea was succeeded by the Baltic Viking era, with seaborne raids by <a href="/wiki/Curonians" title="Curonians">Curonians</a> and by Estonians from the island of <a href="/wiki/Saaremaa" title="Saaremaa">Saaremaa</a>, known as <a href="/wiki/Oeselians" title="Oeselians">Oeselians</a>. In 1187 Estonians (Oeselians), <a href="/wiki/Curonians" title="Curonians">Curonians</a> or/and <a href="/wiki/Karelians" title="Karelians">Karelians</a> <a href="/wiki/Pillage_of_Sigtuna" title="Pillage of Sigtuna">sacked</a> <a href="/wiki/Sigtuna" title="Sigtuna">Sigtuna</a>, which was a major city of Sweden at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tarvel_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tarvel-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the early centuries AD, political and administrative subdivisions began to emerge in Estonia. Two larger subdivisions appeared: the parish (Estonian: <i>kihelkond</i>) and the county (Estonian: <i><a href="/wiki/Maakond" class="mw-redirect" title="Maakond">maakond</a></i>), which consisted of multiple parishes. A parish was led by <a href="/wiki/Elder_(administrative_title)" title="Elder (administrative title)">elders</a> and centred around a hill fort; in some rare cases a parish had multiple forts. By the 13th century Estonia consisted of eight major counties: <a href="/wiki/Harjumaa_(ancient_county)" title="Harjumaa (ancient county)">Harjumaa</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A4rvamaa" class="mw-redirect" title="J\xc3\xa4rvamaa">J\xc3\xa4rvamaa</a>, <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A4%C3%A4nemaa" class="mw-redirect" title="L\xc3\xa4\xc3\xa4nemaa">L\xc3\xa4\xc3\xa4nemaa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Revala" title="Revala">Revala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saare_County" title="Saare County">Saaremaa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sakala_County" title="Sakala County">Sakala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ugandi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ugandi">Ugandi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Virumaa" title="Virumaa">Virumaa</a>; and six minor, single-parish counties: <a href="/wiki/Alempois" title="Alempois">Alempois</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jogentagana" title="Jogentagana">Jogentagana</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B5hu" title="M\xc3\xb5hu">M\xc3\xb5hu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nurmekund" title="Nurmekund">Nurmekund</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soopoolitse" title="Soopoolitse">Soopoolitse</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vaiga" title="Vaiga">Vaiga</a>. Counties were independent entities and engaged only in a loose co-operation against foreign threats.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There is little known of early Estonian <a href="/wiki/Paganism" title="Paganism">pagan</a> religious practices. The <a href="/wiki/Chronicle_of_Henry_of_Livonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Chronicle of Henry of Livonia">Chronicle of Henry of Livonia</a> mentions <a href="/wiki/Tharapita" title="Tharapita">Tharapita</a> as the superior god of the Oeselians. Spiritual practices were guided by <a href="/wiki/Shamans" class="mw-redirect" title="Shamans">shamans</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Sacred_groves" class="mw-redirect" title="Sacred groves">sacred groves</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oak</a> groves, serving as places of worship.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Livonian_Crusade" title="Livonian Crusade">Livonian Crusade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terra_Mariana" title="Terra Mariana">Terra Mariana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Danish_Estonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Danish Estonia">Danish Estonia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Medieval_Livonia_1260.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Medieval_Livonia_1260.svg/220px-Medieval_Livonia_1260.svg.png" width="220" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Medieval_Livonia_1260.svg/330px-Medieval_Livonia_1260.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Medieval_Livonia_1260.svg/440px-Medieval_Livonia_1260.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="955" data-file-height="1034" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Medieval_Livonia_1260.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Medieval Estonia and Livonia after the crusade</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1199 Pope <a href="/wiki/Innocent_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Innocent III">Innocent III</a> declared a <a href="/wiki/Livonian_Crusade" title="Livonian Crusade">crusade</a> to "defend the Christians of Livonia".<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Fighting reached Estonia in 1206, when Danish king <a href="/wiki/Valdemar_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Valdemar II">Valdemar II</a> unsuccessfully invaded Saaremaa. The German <a href="/wiki/Livonian_Brothers_of_the_Sword" title="Livonian Brothers of the Sword">Livonian Brothers of the Sword</a>, who had previously subjugated <a href="/wiki/Livonians" title="Livonians">Livonians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latgalians" title="Latgalians">Latgalians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Selonians" title="Selonians">Selonians</a>, started campaigning against the Estonians in 1208, and over next few years both sides made numerous raids and counter-raids. A major leader of the Estonian resistance was <a href="/wiki/Lembitu" title="Lembitu">Lembitu</a>, an elder of <a href="/wiki/Sakala_County" title="Sakala County">Sakala County</a>, but in 1217 the Estonians suffered a significant defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_St._Matthew%27s_Day" title="Battle of St. Matthew&#39;s Day">Battle of St. Matthew\'s Day</a>, where Lembitu was killed. In 1219, Valdemar II landed at Lindanise, defeated the Estonians in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lyndanisse" title="Battle of Lyndanisse">battle</a>, and started conquering Northern Estonia.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The next year, Sweden invaded Western Estonia, but were <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lihula" title="Battle of Lihula">repelled</a> by the Oeselians. In 1223, a major revolt ejected the Germans and Danes from the whole of Estonia, except <a href="/wiki/Reval" class="mw-redirect" title="Reval">Reval</a>, but the crusaders soon resumed their offensive, and in 1227, Saaremaa was the last county to surrender.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the crusade, the territory of present-day Southern Estonia and Latvia was named <a href="/wiki/Terra_Mariana" title="Terra Mariana">Terra Mariana</a>, but later it became known simply as <a href="/wiki/Livonia" title="Livonia">Livonia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Northern-Estonia became the Danish <a href="/wiki/Danish_Estonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Danish Estonia">Duchy of Estonia</a>, while the rest was divided between the Sword Brothers and <a href="/wiki/Prince-bishopric" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince-bishopric">prince-bishoprics</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Dorpat" title="Bishopric of Dorpat">Dorpat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_%C3%96sel%E2%80%93Wiek" title="Bishopric of \xc3\x96sel\xe2\x80\x93Wiek">\xc3\x96sel\xe2\x80\x93Wiek</a>. In 1236, after suffering a <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Saule" title="Battle of Saule">major defeat</a>, the Sword Brothers merged into the <a href="/wiki/Teutonic_Order" title="Teutonic Order">Teutonic Order</a> becoming the <a href="/wiki/Livonian_Order" title="Livonian Order">Livonian Order</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In the next decades there were several uprisings against foreign rulers on Saaremaa. In 1343, a major rebellion started, known as the <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s_Night_Uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="St. George&#39;s Night Uprising">St. George\'s Night Uprising</a>, encompassing the whole area of Northern-Estonia and Saaremaa. The Teutonic Order finished suppressing the rebellion in 1345, and the next year the Danish king sold his possessions in Estonia to the Order.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The unsuccessful rebellion led to a consolidation of power for the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Germans" title="Baltic Germans">Baltic German</a> minority.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> For the subsequent centuries they remained the ruling elite in both cities and the countryside.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuressaare_Arensburg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Kuressaare Castle, square stone keep with one square corner tower and red tile roof" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Kuressaare_Arensburg.jpg/220px-Kuressaare_Arensburg.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Kuressaare_Arensburg.jpg/330px-Kuressaare_Arensburg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Kuressaare_Arensburg.jpg/440px-Kuressaare_Arensburg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuressaare_Arensburg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kuressaare_Castle" title="Kuressaare Castle">Kuressaare Castle</a> in <a href="/wiki/Saaremaa" title="Saaremaa">Saaremaa</a> dates back to the 1380s.</div></div></div>\n<p>During the crusade, <a href="/wiki/Reval" class="mw-redirect" title="Reval">Reval</a> (Tallinn) was founded, as the capital of Danish Estonia, on the site of Lindanise. In 1248 Reval received full town rights and adopted the <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCbeck_law" title="L\xc3\xbcbeck law">L\xc3\xbcbeck law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a> controlled trade on the Baltic Sea, and overall the four largest towns in Estonia became members: Reval, <a href="/wiki/Dorpat" class="mw-redirect" title="Dorpat">Dorpat</a> (Tartu), <a href="/wiki/Pernau" class="mw-redirect" title="Pernau">Pernau</a> (P\xc3\xa4rnu), and <a href="/wiki/Fellin" class="mw-redirect" title="Fellin">Fellin</a> (Viljandi). Reval acted as a trade intermediary between <a href="/wiki/Novgorod" class="mw-redirect" title="Novgorod">Novgorod</a> and Western Hanseatic cities, while Dorpat filled the same role with <a href="/wiki/Pskov" title="Pskov">Pskov</a>. Many <a href="/wiki/Guilds" class="mw-redirect" title="Guilds">guilds</a> were formed during that period, but only a very few allowed the participation of native Estonians.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Protected by their stone walls and alliance with the Hansa, prosperous cities like Reval and Dorpat repeatedly defied other rulers of Livonia.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> After the decline of the Teutonic Order after its defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grunwald" title="Battle of Grunwald">Battle of Grunwald</a> in 1410, and the defeat of the Livonian Order in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Swienta" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Swienta">Battle of Swienta</a> on 1 September 1435, the <a href="/wiki/Livonian_Confederation" class="mw-redirect" title="Livonian Confederation">Livonian Confederation</a> Agreement was signed on 4 December 1435.<sup id="cite_ref-VLM_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VLM-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Reformation</a> in Europe began in 1517, and soon spread to Livonia despite opposition by the Livonian Order.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Towns were the first to embrace Protestantism in the 1520s, and by the 1530s the majority of the gentry had adopted <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a> for themselves and their peasant serfs.<sup id="cite_ref-Frucht121_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frucht121-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Church services were now conducted in vernacular language, which initially meant German, but in the 1530s the first religious services in <a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a> also took place.<sup id="cite_ref-Frucht121_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frucht121-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 16th century, the expansionist monarchies of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Moscow" title="Grand Duchy of Moscow">Muscowy</a>, Sweden, and <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_union" title="Polish\xe2\x80\x93Lithuanian union">Poland\xe2\x80\x93Lithuania</a> consolidated power, posing a growing threat to decentralised Livonia weakened by disputes between cities, nobility, bishops, and the Order.<sup id="cite_ref-Frucht121_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frucht121-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hoover_Press_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoover_Press-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Swedish_Era">Swedish Era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Swedish Era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Estonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Swedish Estonia">Swedish Estonia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Academia_Gustaviana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Academia_Gustaviana.jpg/220px-Academia_Gustaviana.jpg" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Academia_Gustaviana.jpg/330px-Academia_Gustaviana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Academia_Gustaviana.jpg/440px-Academia_Gustaviana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="773" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Academia_Gustaviana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Academia Dorpatensis" (now <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tartu" title="University of Tartu">University of Tartu</a>) was founded in 1632 by King Gustavus as the second university in the kingdom of Sweden. After the king\'s death it became known as \xe2\x80\x9cAcademia Gustaviana\xe2\x80\x9d.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1558, Tsar <a href="/wiki/Ivan_the_Terrible" title="Ivan the Terrible">Ivan the Terrible</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia">Russia</a> invaded Livonia, starting the <a href="/wiki/Livonian_War" title="Livonian War">Livonian War</a>. The Livonian Order was decisively <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ergeme" title="Battle of Ergeme">defeated</a> in 1560, prompting Livonian factions to seek foreign protection. The majority of Livonia accepted Polish rule, while Reval and the nobles of Northern Estonia swore loyalty to the Swedish king, and the Bishop of \xc3\x96sel-Wiek sold his lands to the Danish king. Russian forces gradually conquered the majority of Livonia, but in the late 1570s the Polish-Lithuanian and Swedish armies started their own offensives and the bloody war finally ended in 1583 with Russian defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoover_Press_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoover_Press-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> As result of the war, Northern Estonia became Swedish <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Estonia_(1561%E2%80%931721)" title="Duchy of Estonia (1561\xe2\x80\x931721)">Duchy of Estonia</a>, Southern Estonia became Polish <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Livonia" title="Duchy of Livonia">Duchy of Livonia</a>, and Saaremaa remained under Danish control.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1600, the <a href="/wiki/Polish-Swedish_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish-Swedish War">Polish-Swedish War</a> broke out, causing further devastation. The protracted war ended in 1629 with Sweden <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Livonia" title="Swedish Livonia">gaining Livonia</a>, including the regions of Southern Estonia and Northern Latvia.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Danish Saaremaa was <a href="/wiki/Second_Treaty_of_Br%C3%B6msebro_(1645)" title="Second Treaty of Br\xc3\xb6msebro (1645)">transferred</a> to Sweden in 1645.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The wars had halved the Estonian population from about 250\xe2\x80\x93270,000 people in the mid 16th century to 115\xe2\x80\x93120,000 in the 1630s.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Serfdom was retained under Swedish rule but legal reforms took place which strengthened peasants\' land usage and inheritance rights, resulting this period\'s reputation of the "Good Old Swedish Time" in people\'s historical memory.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Swedish king <a href="/wiki/Gustavus_Adolphus_of_Sweden" title="Gustavus Adolphus of Sweden">Gustaf II Adolf</a> established <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">gymnasiums</a> in Reval and Dorpat; the latter was upgraded to <a href="/wiki/Tartu_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Tartu University">Tartu University</a> in 1632. <a href="/wiki/Printing_presses" class="mw-redirect" title="Printing presses">Printing presses</a> were also established in both towns. In the 1680s the beginnings of Estonian elementary education appeared, largely due to efforts of <a href="/wiki/Bengt_Gottfried_Forselius" title="Bengt Gottfried Forselius">Bengt Gottfried Forselius</a>, who also introduced orthographical reforms to written Estonian.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The population of Estonia grew rapidly for a 60\xe2\x80\x9370-year period, until the <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_of_Estonia_(1695%E2%80%931697)" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Famine of Estonia (1695\xe2\x80\x931697)">Great Famine</a> of 1695\xe2\x80\x9397 in which some 70,000\xe2\x80\x9375,000 people perished&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 about 20% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_Era_and_National_Awakening">Russian Era and National Awakening</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Russian Era and National Awakening">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Governorate_of_Estonia" title="Governorate of Estonia">Governorate of Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Governorate_of_Livonia" title="Governorate of Livonia">Governorate of Livonia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Estonian_national_awakening" title="Estonian national awakening">Estonian national awakening</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carl_Robert_Jakobson.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Carl_Robert_Jakobson.jpg/150px-Carl_Robert_Jakobson.jpg" width="150" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Carl_Robert_Jakobson.jpg/225px-Carl_Robert_Jakobson.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Carl_Robert_Jakobson.jpg/300px-Carl_Robert_Jakobson.jpg 2x" data-file-width="359" data-file-height="512" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carl_Robert_Jakobson.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Carl_Robert_Jakobson" title="Carl Robert Jakobson">Carl Robert Jakobson</a> played a key role in the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_national_awakening" title="Estonian national awakening">Estonian national awakening</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Perno_Postimeees,_Nr_1.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Perno_Postimeees%2C_Nr_1.png/190px-Perno_Postimeees%2C_Nr_1.png" width="190" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Perno_Postimeees%2C_Nr_1.png/285px-Perno_Postimeees%2C_Nr_1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Perno_Postimeees%2C_Nr_1.png/380px-Perno_Postimeees%2C_Nr_1.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="2781" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Perno_Postimeees,_Nr_1.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The front page of <i><a href="/wiki/P%C3%A4rnu_Postimees" title="P\xc3\xa4rnu Postimees">Perno Postimees</a></i>, the first Estonian language periodical newspaper</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1700, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War" title="Great Northern War">Great Northern War</a> started, and by 1710 the whole of Estonia was conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The war again devastated the population of Estonia, with the 1712 population estimated at only 150,000\xe2\x80\x93170,000.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Russian administration restored all the political and landholding rights of Baltic Germans.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The rights of Estonian peasants reached their lowest point, as serfdom completely dominated agricultural relations during the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Serfdom was formally abolished in 1816\xe2\x80\x931819, but this initially had very little practical effect; major improvements in rights of the peasantry started with reforms in the mid-19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Estonian_national_awakening" title="Estonian national awakening">Estonian national awakening</a> began in the 1850s as the leading figures started promoting an Estonian national identity among the general populace. Its economic basis was formed by widespread farm buyouts by peasants, forming a class of Estonian landowners. In 1857 <a href="/wiki/Johann_Voldemar_Jannsen" title="Johann Voldemar Jannsen">Johann Voldemar Jannsen</a> started publishing the first Estonian language newspaper and began popularising the denomination of oneself as <i>eestlane</i> (Estonian).<sup id="cite_ref-EE286_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EE286-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Schoolmaster <a href="/wiki/Carl_Robert_Jakobson" title="Carl Robert Jakobson">Carl Robert Jakobson</a> and clergyman <a href="/wiki/Jakob_Hurt" title="Jakob Hurt">Jakob Hurt</a> became leading figures in a national movement, encouraging Estonian peasants to take pride in themselves and in their ethnic identity.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The first nationwide movements formed, such as a campaign to establish the Estonian language Alexander School, the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Estonian_Literati" title="Society of Estonian Literati">Society of Estonian Literati</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Students%27_Society" title="Estonian Students&#39; Society">Estonian Students\' Society</a>, and the first <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Song_Festival" title="Estonian Song Festival">national song festival</a>, held in 1869 in Tartu.<sup id="cite_ref-Raun59_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Raun59-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EE287_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EE287-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Linguistic reforms helped to develop the Estonian language.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The national epic <i><a href="/wiki/Kalevipoeg" title="Kalevipoeg">Kalevipoeg</a></i> was published in 1862, and 1870 saw the first performances of <a href="/wiki/Theatre_of_Estonia" title="Theatre of Estonia">Estonian theatre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CoE_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CoE-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> In 1878 a major split happened in the national movement. The moderate wing led by Hurt focused on development of culture and Estonian education, while the radical wing led by Jacobson started demanding increased political and economical rights.<sup id="cite_ref-EE287_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EE287-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the late 19th century the <a href="/wiki/Russification" title="Russification">Russification</a> period started, as the central government initiated various administrative and cultural measures to tie Baltic governorates more closely to the empire.<sup id="cite_ref-Raun59_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Raun59-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The Russian language was used throughout the education system and many Estonian social and cultural activities were suppressed.<sup id="cite_ref-CoE_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CoE-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Still, some administrative changes aimed at reducing power of Baltic German institutions did prove useful to Estonians.<sup id="cite_ref-Raun59_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Raun59-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In the late 1890s there was a new surge of nationalism with the rise of prominent figures like <a href="/wiki/Jaan_T%C3%B5nisson" title="Jaan T\xc3\xb5nisson">Jaan T\xc3\xb5nisson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_P%C3%A4ts" title="Konstantin P\xc3\xa4ts">Konstantin P\xc3\xa4ts</a>. In the early 20th century Estonians started taking over control of local governments in towns from Germans.<sup id="cite_ref-EE291_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EE291-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/1905_Russian_Revolution" title="1905 Russian Revolution">1905 Revolution</a> the first legal Estonian political parties were founded. An Estonian national congress was convened and demanded the unification of Estonian areas into a single autonomous territory and an end to Russification. During the unrest peasants and workers attacked manor houses. The Tsarist government responded with a brutal crackdown; some 500 people were executed and hundreds more were jailed or deported to Siberia.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EE292_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EE292-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Estonia_(1920%E2%80%9339)" title="History of Estonia (1920\xe2\x80\x9339)">History of Estonia (1920\xe2\x80\x9339)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estonian_War_of_Independence" title="Estonian War of Independence">Estonian War of Independence</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Era_of_Silence" title="Era of Silence">Era of Silence</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Declaration_of_Estonian_independence_in_P%C3%A4rnu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="photograph of crowd around flag raising" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Declaration_of_Estonian_independence_in_P%C3%A4rnu.jpg/220px-Declaration_of_Estonian_independence_in_P%C3%A4rnu.jpg" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Declaration_of_Estonian_independence_in_P%C3%A4rnu.jpg/330px-Declaration_of_Estonian_independence_in_P%C3%A4rnu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Declaration_of_Estonian_independence_in_P%C3%A4rnu.jpg/440px-Declaration_of_Estonian_independence_in_P%C3%A4rnu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="691" data-file-height="587" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Declaration_of_Estonian_independence_in_P%C3%A4rnu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Declaration of independence in <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A4rnu" title="P\xc3\xa4rnu">P\xc3\xa4rnu</a> on 23 February 1918. One of the first images of the Republic.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Soomusrong_nr_2_Valgas_1919.jpg" class="image"><img alt="photograph of armoured train" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Soomusrong_nr_2_Valgas_1919.jpg/220px-Soomusrong_nr_2_Valgas_1919.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Soomusrong_nr_2_Valgas_1919.jpg/330px-Soomusrong_nr_2_Valgas_1919.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Soomusrong_nr_2_Valgas_1919.jpg/440px-Soomusrong_nr_2_Valgas_1919.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2183" data-file-height="1413" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Soomusrong_nr_2_Valgas_1919.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Estonian <a href="/wiki/Armoured_train" title="Armoured train">armoured train</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_War_of_Independence" title="Estonian War of Independence">War of Independence</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1917, after the <a href="/wiki/February_Revolution" title="February Revolution">February Revolution</a>, the governorate of Estonia <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Governorate_of_Estonia" title="Autonomous Governorate of Estonia">was expanded</a> to include Estonian speaking areas of Livonia and was granted autonomy, enabling formation of the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Provincial_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Estonian Provincial Assembly">Estonian Provincial Assembly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bolsheviks" title="Bolsheviks">Bolsheviks</a> seized power during the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a>, and disbanded the Provincial Assembly. However the Provincial Assembly established the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Salvation_Committee" title="Estonian Salvation Committee">Salvation Committee</a>, and during the short interlude between Russian retreat and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Faustschlag" title="Operation Faustschlag">German arrival</a>, the committee <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Estonian Declaration of Independence">declared the independence of Estonia</a> on 24 February 1918, and formed the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Provisional_Government" title="Estonian Provisional Government">Estonian Provisional Government</a>. <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Estonia_during_World_War_I" title="German occupation of Estonia during World War I">German occupation</a> immediately followed, but after their defeat in World War I the Germans were forced to hand over power to the Provisional Government on 19 November.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 November 1918 <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet Russia">Soviet Russia</a> invaded, starting the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_War_of_Independence" title="Estonian War of Independence">Estonian War of Independence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> came within 30&#160;km from Tallinn, but in January 1919, the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Estonian Army">Estonian Army</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Johan_Laidoner" title="Johan Laidoner">Johan Laidoner</a>, went on a counter-offensive, ejecting Bolshevik forces from Estonia within a few months. Renewed Soviet attacks failed, and in spring, the Estonian army, in cooperation with <a href="/wiki/White_movement" title="White movement">White Russian</a> forces, advanced into Russia and <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pinder76_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pinder76-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> In June 1919, Estonia <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_C%C4%93sis_(1919)" title="Battle of C\xc4\x93sis (1919)">defeated</a> the <a href="/wiki/Baltische_Landeswehr" title="Baltische Landeswehr">German Landeswehr</a> which had attempted to dominate Latvia, restoring power to the government of <a href="/wiki/K%C4%81rlis_Ulmanis" title="K\xc4\x81rlis Ulmanis">K\xc4\x81rlis Ulmanis</a> there. After the collapse of the White Russian forces, the Red Army launched a <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Krivasoo" title="Battle of Krivasoo">major offensive</a> against Narva in late 1919, but failed to achieve a breakthrough. On 2 February 1920, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tartu_(Russian%E2%80%93Estonian)" title="Treaty of Tartu (Russian\xe2\x80\x93Estonian)">Tartu Peace Treaty</a> was signed between Estonia and Soviet Russia, with the latter pledging to permanently give up all sovereign claims to Estonia.<sup id="cite_ref-Pinder76_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pinder76-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 1919, the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Constituent_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Estonian Constituent Assembly">Estonian Constituent Assembly</a> was elected. The Constituent Assembly passed a sweeping <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Land_Reform_of_1919" title="Estonian Land Reform of 1919">land reform</a> expropriating large estates, and adopted a new highly liberal <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Estonia" title="Constitution of Estonia">constitution</a> establishing Estonia as a <a href="/wiki/Riigikogu" title="Riigikogu">parliamentary</a> democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> In 1924, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> organized a communist <a href="/wiki/1924_Estonian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1924 Estonian coup d&#39;\xc3\xa9tat attempt">coup attempt</a>, which quickly failed.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Estonia\'s cultural autonomy law for ethnic minorities, adopted in 1925, is widely recognized as one of the most liberal in the world at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> put heavy pressure on Estonia\'s political system, and in 1933, the right-wing <a href="/wiki/Vaps_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Vaps movement">Vaps movement</a> spearheaded a constitutional reform establishing a strong presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> On 12 March 1934 the acting head of state, <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_P%C3%A4ts" title="Konstantin P\xc3\xa4ts">Konstantin P\xc3\xa4ts</a>, declared a state of emergency, falsely claiming that the Vaps movement had been planning a coup. P\xc3\xa4ts, together with general Johan Laidoner and <a href="/wiki/Kaarel_Eenpalu" title="Kaarel Eenpalu">Kaarel Eenpalu</a>, established an <a href="/wiki/Era_of_Silence" title="Era of Silence">authoritarian regime</a>, where the parliament was dissolved and the newly established <a href="/wiki/Patriotic_League_(Estonia)" title="Patriotic League (Estonia)">Patriotic League</a> became the only legal political party.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> In order to legitimize the regime, a new constitution was adopted and elections <a href="/wiki/Estonian_parliamentary_election,_1938" title="Estonian parliamentary election, 1938">were held</a> in 1938. Opposition candidates were allowed to participate, but only as independents, while opposition parties remained banned.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> The P\xc3\xa4ts regime was relatively benign compared to other authoritarian regimes in <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">interwar</a> Europe, and there was no systematic terror against political opponents.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Estonia joined the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> in 1921.<sup id="cite_ref-Ginneken_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ginneken-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Attempts to establish a <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Accord" title="Warsaw Accord">larger alliance</a> together with <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">Poland</a>, and Latvia failed, with only a mutual defence pact being signed with Latvia in 1923, and later was followed up with the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Entente" title="Baltic Entente">Baltic Entente</a> of 1934.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> In the 1930s, Estonia also engaged in <a href="/wiki/Finnish%E2%80%93Estonian_defence_cooperation" title="Finnish\xe2\x80\x93Estonian defence cooperation">secret military cooperation</a> with Finland.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Non-aggression pacts were signed <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Estonian_Non-Aggression_Pact" title="Soviet\xe2\x80\x93Estonian Non-Aggression Pact">with the Soviet Union</a> in 1932, and <a href="/wiki/German%E2%80%93Estonian_Non-Aggression_Pact" title="German\xe2\x80\x93Estonian Non-Aggression Pact">with Germany</a> in 1939.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ginneken_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ginneken-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> In 1938, Estonia declared neutrality, but this proved futile in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Red_Army_entering_into_Estonia_in_1939.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Red_Army_entering_into_Estonia_in_1939.jpg/220px-Red_Army_entering_into_Estonia_in_1939.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Red_Army_entering_into_Estonia_in_1939.jpg/330px-Red_Army_entering_into_Estonia_in_1939.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Red_Army_entering_into_Estonia_in_1939.jpg/440px-Red_Army_entering_into_Estonia_in_1939.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1736" data-file-height="1205" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Red_Army_entering_into_Estonia_in_1939.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> entering Estonia in 1939 after Estonia had been forced to sign the <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Estonian_Mutual_Assistance_Treaty" title="Soviet\xe2\x80\x93Estonian Mutual Assistance Treaty">Bases Treaty</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Estonia_in_World_War_II" title="Estonia in World War II">Estonia in World War II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Baltic_states" title="Occupation of the Baltic states">Occupation of the Baltic states</a></div>\n<p>On 23 August 1939 <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> and the Soviet Union signed the <a href="/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov\xe2\x80\x93Ribbentrop Pact">Molotov\xe2\x80\x93Ribbentrop Pact</a>. The pact\'s secret protocol divided Eastern-Europe into spheres of influence, with Estonia belonging to the Soviet sphere.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> On 24 September, the Soviet Union presented an ultimatum, demanding that Estonia sign a treaty of mutual assistance which would allow Soviet military bases into the country. The Estonian government felt that it had no choice but to comply, and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Estonian_Mutual_Assistance_Treaty" title="Soviet\xe2\x80\x93Estonian Mutual Assistance Treaty">treaty was signed</a> on 28 September.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> In May 1940, Red Army forces in bases were set in combat readiness and, on 14 June, the Soviet Union instituted a full naval and air blockade on Estonia. On the same day, the airliner <a href="/wiki/Kaleva_(airplane)" title="Kaleva (airplane)">Kaleva</a> was shot down by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Air_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet Air Force">Soviet Air Force</a>. On 16 June, Soviets presented an ultimatum demanding completely free passage of the Red Army into Estonia and the establishment of a pro-Soviet government. Feeling that resistance was hopeless, the Estonian government complied and, on the next day, the whole country was occupied.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> On 6 August 1940, Estonia was annexed by the Soviet Union as the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Estonian SSR">Estonian SSR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-malksoo_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malksoo-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Soviets established a regime of oppression; most of the high-ranking civil and military officials, intelligentsia and industrialists were arrested, and usually executed soon afterwards. Soviet repressions culminated on 14 June 1941 with <a href="/wiki/June_deportation" title="June deportation">mass deportation</a> of about 11,000 people to <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, among whom more than half perished in inhumane conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-Miljan110_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miljan110-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> When the German <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">Operation Barbarossa</a> started against the Soviet Union on 22 June 1941, about 34,000 young Estonian men were forcibly drafted into the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a>, fewer than 30% of whom survived the war. Soviet <a href="/wiki/Destruction_battalions" title="Destruction battalions">destruction battalions</a> initiated a scorched earth policy. Political prisoners who could not be evacuated <a href="/wiki/NKVD_prisoner_massacres" title="NKVD prisoner massacres">were executed</a> by the <a href="/wiki/NKVD" title="NKVD">NKVD</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Many Estonians <a href="/wiki/Forest_Brothers" title="Forest Brothers">went into the forest</a>, starting an anti-Soviet guerrilla campaign. In July, German <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a> reached south Estonia. Soviets <a href="/wiki/Soviet_evacuation_of_Tallinn" title="Soviet evacuation of Tallinn">evacuated Tallinn</a> in late August with massive losses, and capture of the Estonian islands was completed by German forces in October.<sup id="cite_ref-pinder80_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pinder80-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TLA_1465_1_973_Varemetes_Harju_t%C3%A4nav,_vasakul_Kuld_L%C3%B5vi_varemed_1944.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/TLA_1465_1_973_Varemetes_Harju_t%C3%A4nav%2C_vasakul_Kuld_L%C3%B5vi_varemed_1944.jpg/220px-TLA_1465_1_973_Varemetes_Harju_t%C3%A4nav%2C_vasakul_Kuld_L%C3%B5vi_varemed_1944.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/TLA_1465_1_973_Varemetes_Harju_t%C3%A4nav%2C_vasakul_Kuld_L%C3%B5vi_varemed_1944.jpg/330px-TLA_1465_1_973_Varemetes_Harju_t%C3%A4nav%2C_vasakul_Kuld_L%C3%B5vi_varemed_1944.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/TLA_1465_1_973_Varemetes_Harju_t%C3%A4nav%2C_vasakul_Kuld_L%C3%B5vi_varemed_1944.jpg/440px-TLA_1465_1_973_Varemetes_Harju_t%C3%A4nav%2C_vasakul_Kuld_L%C3%B5vi_varemed_1944.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8450" data-file-height="5680" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TLA_1465_1_973_Varemetes_Harju_t%C3%A4nav,_vasakul_Kuld_L%C3%B5vi_varemed_1944.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The old town of Tallinn after <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Tallinn_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Tallinn in World War II">bombing by the Soviet Air Force</a> in March 1944</div></div></div>\n<p>Initially many Estonians were hopeful that Germany would help to restore Estonia\'s independence, but this soon proved to be in vain. Only a puppet <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Self-Administration" title="Estonian Self-Administration">collaborationist administration</a> was established, and <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Estonia_during_World_War_II" title="German occupation of Estonia during World War II">occupied Estonia</a> was merged into <a href="/wiki/Reichskommissariat_Ostland" title="Reichskommissariat Ostland">Reichskommissariat Ostland</a>, with its economy being fully subjugated to German military needs.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> About a thousand <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Estonian Jews">Estonian Jews</a> who had not managed to leave were almost all <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_in_Estonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust in Estonia">quickly killed</a> in 1941. Numerous forced labour camps were established where thousands of Estonians, foreign Jews, <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani</a>, and <a href="/wiki/German_mistreatment_of_Soviet_prisoners_of_war" title="German mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war">Soviet prisoners of war</a> perished.<sup id="cite_ref-CommissionReport_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CommissionReport-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> German occupation authorities started recruiting men into small <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Legion" title="Estonian Legion">volunteer units</a> but, as these efforts provided meagre results and military situation worsened, a forced conscription was instituted in 1943, eventually leading to formation of the <a href="/wiki/20th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_(1st_Estonian)" title="20th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (1st Estonian)">Estonian Waffen-SS division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Thousands of Estonians who did not want to fight in German military secretly escaped to Finland, where <a
