href="/wiki/Finnish_Infantry_Regiment_200" title="Finnish Infantry Regiment 200">many volunteered</a> to fight together with Finns <a href="/wiki/Continuation_War" title="Continuation War">against Soviets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Red Army reached the Estonian borders again in early 1944, but its advance into Estonia was stopped in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Narva_(1944)" title="Battle of Narva (1944)">heavy fighting near Narva</a> for six months by German forces, including numerous Estonian units.<sup id="cite_ref-Raun159_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Raun159-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> In March, the Soviet Air Force carried out heavy bombing raids <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Tallinn_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Tallinn in World War II">against Tallinn</a> and other Estonian towns.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> In July, the Soviets started <a href="/wiki/Tallinn_Offensive" title="Tallinn Offensive">a major offensive</a> from the south, forcing the Germans to abandon mainland Estonia in September, with the Estonian islands being abandoned in November.<sup id="cite_ref-Raun159_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Raun159-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> As German forces were retreating from Tallinn, the last pre-war prime minister <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCri_Uluots" title="J\xc3\xbcri Uluots">J\xc3\xbcri Uluots</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Committee_of_the_Republic_of_Estonia" title="National Committee of the Republic of Estonia">appointed a government</a> headed by <a href="/wiki/Otto_Tief" title="Otto Tief">Otto Tief</a> in an unsuccessful attempt restore Estonia\'s independence.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Tens of thousands of people, including most of the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Swedes" title="Estonian Swedes">Estonian Swedes</a>, fled westwards to avoid the new Soviet occupation.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Estlandssvenska_flyktingar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="sailing ship filled with refugees" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Estlandssvenska_flyktingar.jpg/220px-Estlandssvenska_flyktingar.jpg" width="220" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Estlandssvenska_flyktingar.jpg/330px-Estlandssvenska_flyktingar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Estlandssvenska_flyktingar.jpg/440px-Estlandssvenska_flyktingar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2760" data-file-height="1425" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Estlandssvenska_flyktingar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Estonian_Swedes" title="Estonian Swedes">Estonian Swedes</a> fleeing the Soviet occupation to Sweden (1944)</div></div></div>\n<p>Overall, Estonia lost about 25% of its population through deaths, deportations and evacuations in World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Estonia also suffered some permanent territorial losses, as Soviet Union transferred border areas comprising about 5% of Estonian pre-war territory from the Estonian SSR to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_SFSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian SFSR">Russian SFSR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_Period">Soviet Period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Soviet Period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Estonian Soviet Socialist Republic">Estonian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Baltic_states" title="Occupation of the Baltic states">Occupation of the Baltic states</a></div>\n<p>Thousands of Estonians opposing the second Soviet occupation joined a guerrilla movement known as <a href="/wiki/Forest_Brothers" title="Forest Brothers">Forest Brothers</a>. The armed resistance was heaviest in the first few years after the war, but Soviet authorities gradually wore it down through attrition, and resistance effectively ceased to exist in the mid 1950s.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The Soviets initiated a <a href="/wiki/Collectivization_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Collectivization in the Soviet Union">policy of collectivization</a>, but as peasants remained opposed to it a campaign of terror was unleashed. In March 1949 about 20,000 Estonians <a href="/wiki/Operation_Priboi" title="Operation Priboi">were deported</a> to Siberia. Collectivization was fully completed soon afterwards.<sup id="cite_ref-Miljan110_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miljan110-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Soviet Union began <a href="/wiki/Russification" title="Russification">Russification</a>, with hundreds of thousands of <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Estonia" title="Russians in Estonia">Russians</a> being induced to settle in Estonia, which eventually threatened to turn Estonians into a minority in their own land.<sup id="cite_ref-Taagepera97_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taagepera97-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> In early 1945 Estonians formed 94% of the population, but by 1989 their share of the population had fallen to 61.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Economically, heavy industry was strongly prioritized, but this did not improve the well-being of the local population, and caused massive environmental damage through pollution.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Living standards under the Soviet occupation kept falling further behind nearby independent Finland.<sup id="cite_ref-Taagepera97_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taagepera97-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The country was heavily militarized, with closed military areas covering 2% of territory.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Islands and most of the coastal areas were turned into a restricted border zone which required a special permit for entry.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The United States, United Kingdom, France, Germany, and the majority of other Western countries <a href="/wiki/Stimson_Doctrine" title="Stimson Doctrine">considered</a> the annexation of Estonia by the Soviet Union illegal.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/State_continuity_of_the_Baltic_states" title="State continuity of the Baltic states">Legal continuity</a> of the Estonian state was preserved through the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_government-in-exile" title="Estonian government-in-exile">government-in-exile</a> and the Estonian <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Diplomatic_Service_(1940%E2%80%9391)" title="Estonian Diplomatic Service (1940\xe2\x80\x9391)">diplomatic representatives</a> which Western governments continued to recognize.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Restoration_of_Independence">Restoration of Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Restoration of Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Singing_Revolution" title="Singing Revolution">Singing Revolution</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lennart_Meri_1998.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Lennart_Meri_1998.jpg/150px-Lennart_Meri_1998.jpg" width="150" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Lennart_Meri_1998.jpg/225px-Lennart_Meri_1998.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Lennart_Meri_1998.jpg/300px-Lennart_Meri_1998.jpg 2x" data-file-width="573" data-file-height="900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lennart_Meri_1998.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lennart_Meri" title="Lennart Meri">Lennart Meri</a> became the president of Estonia after the restoration of independence.</div></div></div>\n<p>The introduction of <a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">Perestroika</a> in 1987 made political activity possible again, starting an independence restoration process known as the <a href="/wiki/Singing_Revolution" title="Singing Revolution">Singing Revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The environmental <a href="/wiki/Phosphorite_War" title="Phosphorite War">Phosphorite War</a> campaign became the first major protest movement against the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Government of the Soviet Union">central government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> In 1988 new political movements appeared, such as the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Front_of_Estonia" title="Popular Front of Estonia">Popular Front of Estonia</a> which came to represent the moderate wing in the independence movement, and the more radical <a href="/wiki/Estonian_National_Independence_Party" title="Estonian National Independence Party">Estonian National Independence Party</a>, which was the first non-communist party in the Soviet Union and demanded full restoration of independence.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Reformist <a href="/wiki/Vaino_V%C3%A4ljas" title="Vaino V\xc3\xa4ljas">Vaino V\xc3\xa4ljas</a> became the first secretary of Estonian Communist Party, and under his leadership on 16 November 1988 Estonian <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Soviet" title="Supreme Soviet">Supreme Soviet</a> issued <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Sovereignty_Declaration" title="Estonian Sovereignty Declaration">Sovereignty Declaration</a> asserting the primacy of Estonian laws over Union laws. Over the next two years almost all other <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">Soviet Republics</a> followed the Estonian lead issuing similar declarations.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> On 23 August 1989 about 2 million Estonians, Latvians and Lithuanians participated in a mass demonstration forming a <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Way" title="Baltic Way">Baltic Way</a> human chain across the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">three republics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> In 1990 the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Estonia" title="Congress of Estonia">Congress of Estonia</a> was formed as representative body of Estonian citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> In March 1991 a <a href="/wiki/Estonian_independence_referendum,_1991" title="Estonian independence referendum, 1991">referendum was held</a> where 77.7% of voters supported independence, and during the <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d&#39;\xc3\xa9tat attempt">coup attempt in Moscow</a> Estonia <a href="/wiki/Estonian_restoration_of_Independence" title="Estonian restoration of Independence">declared restoration of independence</a> on 20 August,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> which is now the Day of Restoration of Independence, a <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Estonia" title="Public holidays in Estonia">national holiday</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Soviet authorities recognized Estonian independence on 6 September, and on 17 September Estonia was admitted into the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dillon164_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dillon164-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The last units of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_army" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian army">Russian army</a> left Estonia in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1992 radical economic reforms were launched for switching over to a market economy, including privatisation and currency reform.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Estonian foreign policy since independence has been orientated towards <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">the West</a>, and in 2004 Estonia joined both the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Territorial_history_timeline">Territorial history timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Territorial history timeline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div style="text-align: center;">\n<table style="border:0px background-color:#f7f8ff; padding:0px;" align="center">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td>\n<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_3fb2f2b8fbf9d08023a1a5a10402dee0"><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/Livonian_Confederation" coords="279,59,437,80" title="Livonian Confederation" alt="Livonian Confederation" /><area shape="rect" href="/wiki/Terra_Mariana" coords="97,86,205,107" title="Terra Mariana" alt="Terra Mariana" /><area shape="rect" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/3fb2f2b8fbf9d08023a1a5a10402dee0.png" /></div>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Estonia" title="Geography of Estonia">Geography of Estonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Estonia" title="Climate of Estonia">Climate of Estonia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Panga_pank-2-mauricedb.jpg" class="image"><img alt="limestone cliffs at the shore with clouds" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Panga_pank-2-mauricedb.jpg/180px-Panga_pank-2-mauricedb.jpg" width="180" height="284" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Panga_pank-2-mauricedb.jpg/270px-Panga_pank-2-mauricedb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Panga_pank-2-mauricedb.jpg/360px-Panga_pank-2-mauricedb.jpg 2x" data-file-width="649" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Panga_pank-2-mauricedb.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The northern coast of Estonia consists mainly of <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> cliffs.</div></div></div>\n<p>Estonia lies on the eastern shores of the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> immediately across the Gulf of Finland from Finland on the level northwestern part of the rising <a href="/wiki/East_European_platform" class="mw-redirect" title="East European platform">East European platform</a> between 57.3\xc2\xb0 and 59.5\xc2\xb0&#160;N and 21.5\xc2\xb0 and 28.1\xc2\xb0&#160;E. Average elevation reaches only 50 metres (164&#160;ft) and the country\'s highest point is the <a href="/wiki/Suur_Munam%C3%A4gi" title="Suur Munam\xc3\xa4gi">Suur Munam\xc3\xa4gi</a> in the southeast at 318 metres (1,043&#160;ft). There is 3,794 kilometres (2,357&#160;mi) of coastline marked by numerous bays, straits, and inlets. The number of islands and islets is estimated at some 2,355 (including those in lakes). Two of them are large enough to constitute separate counties: <a href="/wiki/Saaremaa" title="Saaremaa">Saaremaa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hiiumaa" title="Hiiumaa">Hiiumaa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-worldinfo_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldinfo-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-worldinfoEstonia_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldinfoEstonia-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> A small, recent cluster of meteorite craters, the largest of which is called <a href="/wiki/Kaali_crater" title="Kaali crater">Kaali</a> is found on Saaremaa, Estonia.\n</p><p>Estonia is situated in the northern part of the <a href="/wiki/Temperate" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperate">temperate climate zone</a> and in the transition zone between <a href="/wiki/Maritime_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritime climate">maritime</a> and <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification#Group_D:_Continental/microthermal_climates" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">continental climate</a>. Estonia has four seasons of near-equal length. Average temperatures range from 16.3&#160;\xc2\xb0C (61.3&#160;\xc2\xb0F) on the islands to 18.1&#160;\xc2\xb0C (64.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F) inland in July, the warmest month, and from \xe2\x88\x923.5&#160;\xc2\xb0C (25.7&#160;\xc2\xb0F) on the islands to \xe2\x88\x927.6&#160;\xc2\xb0C (18.3&#160;\xc2\xb0F) inland in February, the coldest month. The average annual temperature in Estonia is 5.2&#160;\xc2\xb0C (41.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-EMHI_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EMHI-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The average precipitation in 1961\xe2\x80\x931990 ranged from 535 to 727&#160;mm (21.1 to 28.6&#160;in) per year.<sup id="cite_ref-emhi2_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emhi2-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Snow cover, which is deepest in the south-eastern part of Estonia, usually lasts from mid-December to late March. Estonia has over <a href="/wiki/List_of_lakes_in_Estonia" class="mw-redirect" title="List of lakes in Estonia">1,400 lakes</a>. Most are very small, with the largest, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Peipus" title="Lake Peipus">Lake Peipus</a>, being 3,555&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (1,373&#160;sq&#160;mi). There are many rivers in the country. The longest of them are V\xc3\xb5handu (162&#160;km or 101&#160;mi), P\xc3\xa4rnu (144&#160;km or 89&#160;mi), and P\xc3\xb5ltsamaa (135&#160;km or 84&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-worldinfo_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldinfo-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Estonia has numerous <a href="/wiki/Fen" title="Fen">fens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bogs" class="mw-redirect" title="Bogs">bogs</a>. Forest land covers 50% of Estonia.<sup id="cite_ref-timber_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timber-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> The most common tree species are pine, spruce and birch.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">Phytogeographically</a>, Estonia is shared between the Central European and Eastern European provinces of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">WWF</a>, the territory of Estonia belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sarmatic_mixed_forests" title="Sarmatic mixed forests">Sarmatic mixed forests</a>.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303619">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .mw-module-gallery{display:block!important;float:none!important}.mw-parser-output .mw-module-gallery srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Roosa_hommikuudu_Tolkuse_rabas.jpg/270px-Roosa_hommikuudu_Tolkuse_rabas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Roosa_hommikuudu_Tolkuse_rabas.jpg/360px-Roosa_hommikuudu_Tolkuse_rabas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5000" data-file-height="3333" /></a></div></div></div></div><div style="display:table-row;vertical-align:top"><div style="display:block;font-size:94%;padding:0px"><div class="gallerytext" style="min-height:6.1em;width:187px;line-height:1.3em;padding:2px 6px 1px 6px;margin:0px;border:none;border-width:0px">There are approximately 2,549 square kilometres (984&#160;sq&#160;mi) of <a href="/wiki/Mire" title="Mire">mires</a> in Estonia which cover 5.6% of the territory.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>&#160;</div></div></div></div><div style="display:table;width:200px;float:left;border-collapse:collapse;margin:3px"><div style="display:table-row"><div style="display:table-cell;height:170px;border:1px solid #CCCCCC;background-color:#F8F8F8;padding:0px;text-align:center"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Haanja_2010_01_1.jpg" class="image" title="50% of Estonia&#39;s territory is covered by forest land."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Haanja_2010_01_1.jpg/180px-Haanja_2010_01_1.jpg" width="180" height="119" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Haanja_2010_01_1.jpg/270px-Haanja_2010_01_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Haanja_2010_01_1.jpg/360px-Haanja_2010_01_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2653" /></a></div></div></div></div><div style="display:table-row;vertical-align:top"><div style="display:block;font-size:94%;padding:0px"><div class="gallerytext" style="min-height:6.1em;width:187px;line-height:1.3em;padding:2px 6px 1px 6px;margin:0px;border:none;border-width:0px">50% of Estonia\'s territory is covered by forest land.&#160;</div></div></div></div><div style="display:table;width:200px;float:left;border-collapse:collapse;margin:3px"><div style="display:table-row"><div style="display:table-cell;height:170px;border:1px solid #CCCCCC;background-color:#F8F8F8;padding:0px;text-align:center"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Hommik_Viru_rabas.jpg" class="image" title="Duckboards along a hiking trail in Viru bog in Lahemaa National Park. The longest hiking trail is 627&#160;km (390&#160;mi) long."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Hommik_Viru_rabas.jpg/180px-Hommik_Viru_rabas.jpg" width="180" height="120" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Hommik_Viru_rabas.jpg/270px-Hommik_Viru_rabas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Hommik_Viru_rabas.jpg/360px-Hommik_Viru_rabas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7298" data-file-height="4871" /></a></div></div></div></div><div style="display:table-row;vertical-align:top"><div style="display:block;font-size:94%;padding:0px"><div class="gallerytext" style="min-height:6.1em;width:187px;line-height:1.3em;padding:2px 6px 1px 6px;margin:0px;border:none;border-width:0px">Duckboards along a hiking trail in Viru bog in <a href="/wiki/Lahemaa_National_Park" title="Lahemaa National Park">Lahemaa National Park</a>. The longest hiking trail is 627&#160;km (390&#160;mi) long.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>&#160;</div></div></div></div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_Estonia" title="Fauna of Estonia">Fauna of Estonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Estonia" title="Protected areas of Estonia">Protected areas of Estonia</a></div>\n<p>Many species extinct in most of the European countries can be still found in Estonia. Mammals present in Estonia include the <a href="/wiki/Grey_wolf" class="mw-redirect" title="Grey wolf">grey wolf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_lynx" title="Eurasian lynx">lynx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brown_bear" title="Brown bear">brown bear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roe_deer" title="Roe deer">roe deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elk" title="Elk">elk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grey_seal" title="Grey seal">grey seal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ringed_seal" title="Ringed seal">ringed seal</a>. Critically endangered <a href="/wiki/European_mink" title="European mink">European mink</a> has been successfully reintroduced to the <a href="/wiki/Hiiumaa" title="Hiiumaa">Hiiumaa</a> island, and the rare <a href="/wiki/Siberian_flying_squirrel" title="Siberian flying squirrel">Siberian flying squirrel</a> is present in east Estonia.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Over 300 bird species have been found in Estonia, including the <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_eagle" title="White-tailed eagle">white-tailed eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lesser_spotted_eagle" title="Lesser spotted eagle">lesser spotted eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_eagle" title="Golden eagle">golden eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_capercaillie" title="Western capercaillie">western capercaillie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_Stork" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Stork">black</a> and <a href="/wiki/White_stork" title="White stork">white stork</a>, numerous species of <a href="/wiki/Owls" class="mw-redirect" title="Owls">owls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wader" title="Wader">waders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geese" class="mw-redirect" title="Geese">geese</a> and many others.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Barn_swallow" title="Barn swallow">Barn swallow</a> is the <a href="/wiki/National_bird" class="mw-redirect" title="National bird">national bird</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Estonia" title="Protected areas of Estonia">Protected areas</a> cover 18% of Estonian land and 26% of its sea territory. There are 5 national parks, 159 nature reserves, and many other protection areas.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Estonia" title="Politics of Estonia">Politics of Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Estonia" title="List of political parties in Estonia">List of political parties in Estonia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Estonia" title="Elections in Estonia">Elections in Estonia</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:left; float:right; margin-right:9px; margin-left:2px;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/File:In%C4%81ra_M%C5%ABrniece_tiekas_ar_Igaunijas_prezidenti_(croped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="In\xc4\x81ra M\xc5\xabrniece tiekas ar Igaunijas prezidenti (croped).jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/In%C4%81ra_M%C5%ABrniece_tiekas_ar_Igaunijas_prezidenti_%28croped%29.jpg/143px-In%C4%81ra_M%C5%ABrniece_tiekas_ar_Igaunijas_prezidenti_%28croped%29.jpg" width="143" height="190" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/In%C4%81ra_M%C5%ABrniece_tiekas_ar_Igaunijas_prezidenti_%28croped%29.jpg/214px-In%C4%81ra_M%C5%ABrniece_tiekas_ar_Igaunijas_prezidenti_%28croped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/In%C4%81ra_M%C5%ABrniece_tiekas_ar_Igaunijas_prezidenti_%28croped%29.jpg/285px-In%C4%81ra_M%C5%ABrniece_tiekas_ar_Igaunijas_prezidenti_%28croped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="714" data-file-height="950" /></a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/File:RK_J%C3%BCri_Ratas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="RK J\xc3\xbcri Ratas.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/RK_J%C3%BCri_Ratas.jpg/136px-RK_J%C3%BCri_Ratas.jpg" width="136" height="190" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/RK_J%C3%BCri_Ratas.jpg/203px-RK_J%C3%BCri_Ratas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/RK_J%C3%BCri_Ratas.jpg/271px-RK_J%C3%BCri_Ratas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1999" data-file-height="2799" /></a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Kersti_Kaljulaid" title="Kersti Kaljulaid">Kersti Kaljulaid</a><br /><small><a href="/wiki/President_of_Estonia" title="President of Estonia">President</a> since 2016</small>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCri_Ratas" title="J\xc3\xbcri Ratas">J\xc3\xbcri Ratas</a><br /><small><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Estonia" title="Prime Minister of Estonia">Prime Minister</a> since 2016</small>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Estonia is a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> republic in which the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Estonia" title="Prime Minister of Estonia">Prime Minister of Estonia</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> and which includes a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. The political culture is stable in Estonia, where power is held between two and three parties that have been in politics for a long time. This situation is similar to other countries in Northern Europe. The former Prime Minister of Estonia, <a href="/wiki/Andrus_Ansip" title="Andrus Ansip">Andrus Ansip</a>, is also Europe\'s longest-serving Prime Minister (from 2005 until 2014). The current Estonian Prime Minister is <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCri_Ratas" title="J\xc3\xbcri Ratas">J\xc3\xbcri Ratas</a>, who is the former Second Vice-President of the Parliament and the head of the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Centre_Party" title="Estonian Centre Party">Estonian Centre Party</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliament">Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Riigikogu" title="Riigikogu">Riigikogu</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Riigikogu_hoone,_Kaupo_Kalda_foto,_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Toompea Castle pink stucco three-story building with red hip roof" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Riigikogu_hoone%2C_Kaupo_Kalda_foto%2C_2016.jpg/220px-Riigikogu_hoone%2C_Kaupo_Kalda_foto%2C_2016.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Riigikogu_hoone%2C_Kaupo_Kalda_foto%2C_2016.jpg/330px-Riigikogu_hoone%2C_Kaupo_Kalda_foto%2C_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Riigikogu_hoone%2C_Kaupo_Kalda_foto%2C_2016.jpg/440px-Riigikogu_hoone%2C_Kaupo_Kalda_foto%2C_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4600" data-file-height="3448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Riigikogu_hoone,_Kaupo_Kalda_foto,_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The seat of the Parliament of Estonia in <a href="/wiki/Toompea_Castle" title="Toompea Castle">Toompea Castle</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Parliament of Estonia (<a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a>: <i lang="et"><a href="/wiki/Riigikogu" title="Riigikogu">Riigikogu</a></i>) or the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">legislative branch</a> is elected by people for a four-year term by <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>. The Estonian political system operates under a framework laid out in the 1992 <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">constitutional document</a>. The Estonian parliament has 101 members and influences the governing of the state primarily by determining the income and the expenses of the state (establishing taxes and adopting the budget). At the same time the parliament has the right to present statements, declarations and appeals to the people of Estonia, ratify and denounce international treaties with other states and international organisations and decide on the Government loans.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Riigikogu elects and appoints several high officials of the state, including the President of the Republic. In addition to that, the Riigikogu appoints, on the proposal of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Estonia" title="President of Estonia">President of Estonia</a>, the Chairman of the National Court, the chairman of the board of the Bank of Estonia, the Auditor General, the Legal Chancellor and the Commander-in-Chief of the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Defence_Forces" title="Estonian Defence Forces">Defence Forces</a>. A member of the Riigikogu has the right to demand explanations from the Government of the Republic and its members. This enables the members of the parliament to observe the activities of the executive power and the above-mentioned high officials of the state.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Estonia" title="Government of Estonia">Government of Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Estonia" title="Prime Minister of Estonia">Prime Minister of Estonia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/President_of_Estonia" title="President of Estonia">President of Estonia</a></div>\n<p>The Government of Estonia (<a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a>: <i lang="et">Vabariigi Valitsus</i>) or the <a href="/wiki/Executive_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive branch">executive branch</a> is formed by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Estonia" title="Prime Minister of Estonia">Prime Minister of Estonia</a>, nominated by the president and approved by the parliament. The government exercises executive power pursuant to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Estonia" title="Constitution of Estonia">Constitution of Estonia</a> and the laws of the Republic of Estonia and consists of twelve ministers, including the Prime Minister. The Prime Minister also has the right to appoint other ministers and assign them a subject to deal with. These are <i>ministers without portfolio</i> \xe2\x80\x93 they don\'t have a ministry to control.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stenbock_House.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Stenbock House grey stucco three-story building with pediment and portico and red hip roof" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Stenbock_House.jpg/220px-Stenbock_House.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Stenbock_House.jpg/330px-Stenbock_House.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Stenbock_House.jpg/440px-Stenbock_House.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stenbock_House.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Stenbock_House" title="Stenbock House">Stenbock House</a>, the seat of the Government of Estonia on <a href="/wiki/Toompea" title="Toompea">Toompea</a> Hill</div></div></div>\n<p>The Prime Minister has the right to appoint a maximum of three such ministers, as the limit of ministers in one government is fifteen. It is also known as the cabinet. The cabinet carries out the country\'s domestic and foreign policy, shaped by parliament; it directs and co-ordinates the work of government institutions and bears full responsibility for everything occurring within the authority of executive power. The government, headed by the Prime Minister, thus represents the political leadership of the country and makes decisions in the name of the whole executive power.\n</p><p>Estonia has pursued the development of the e-state and <a href="/wiki/E-government" title="E-government">e-government</a>. <a href="/wiki/Electronic_voting" title="Electronic voting">Internet voting</a> is used in elections in Estonia.<sup id="cite_ref-news.cnet.com_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.cnet.com-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> The first internet voting took place in the 2005 local elections and the first in a parliamentary election was made available for the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_parliamentary_election,_2007" title="Estonian parliamentary election, 2007">2007 elections</a>, in which 30,275 individuals voted over the internet. Voters have a chance to invalidate their electronic vote in traditional elections, if they wish to. In 2009 in its eighth Worldwide Press Freedom Index, <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a> ranked Estonia sixth out of 175 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> In the first ever <a href="/wiki/State_of_World_Liberty_Index" title="State of World Liberty Index">State of World Liberty Index</a> report, Estonia was ranked first out of 159 countries.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Law">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Estonia" title="Law of Estonia">Law of Estonia</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Police_and_Border_Guard_Board" title="Police and Border Guard Board">Police and Border Guard Board</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Piirivalve_mootorkelgud.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Huey helicopter landing on a pad next to a wetland" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Piirivalve_mootorkelgud.jpg/220px-Piirivalve_mootorkelgud.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Piirivalve_mootorkelgud.jpg/330px-Piirivalve_mootorkelgud.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Piirivalve_mootorkelgud.jpg/440px-Piirivalve_mootorkelgud.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3100" data-file-height="2067" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Piirivalve_mootorkelgud.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Estonian_Border_Guard" title="Estonian Border Guard">Estonian Border Guard</a></div></div></div>\n<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Estonia" title="Constitution of Estonia">Constitution of Estonia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a>: <i lang="et">P\xc3\xb5hiseadus</i>) the supreme power of the state is vested in the people. The people exercise their supreme power of the state on the elections of the Riigikogu through citizens who have the right to vote.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The supreme <a href="/wiki/Judicial_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Judicial power">judicial power</a> is vested in the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Estonia" title="Supreme Court of Estonia">Supreme Court</a> or <a href="/wiki/Riigikohus" class="mw-redirect" title="Riigikohus">Riigikohus</a>, with nineteen justices.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> The Chief Justice is appointed by the parliament for nine years on nomination by the president. The official <a href="/wiki/Head_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Head of State">Head of State</a> is the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Estonia" title="President of Estonia">President of Estonia</a>, who gives assent to the laws passed by <a href="/wiki/Riigikogu" title="Riigikogu">Riigikogu</a>, also having the right of <a href="/wiki/President_of_Estonia#Veto_power" title="President of Estonia">sending them back</a> and proposing new laws.\n</p><p>The President, however, does not use these rights very often, having a largely ceremonial role.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> He or she is elected by Riigikogu, with two-thirds of the votes required. If the candidate does not gain the amount of votes required, the right to elect the President goes over to an electoral body, consisting of the 101 members of Riigikogu and representatives from local councils. As in other spheres, Estonian law-making has been successfully integrated with the <a href="/wiki/Information_Age" title="Information Age">Information Age</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Estonia" title="Counties of Estonia">Counties of Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Estonia" title="Municipalities of Estonia">Municipalities of Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boroughs_of_Estonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Boroughs of Estonia">Boroughs of Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Small_boroughs_of_Estonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Small boroughs of Estonia">Small boroughs of Estonia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Populated_places_in_Estonia" title="Populated places in Estonia">Populated places in Estonia</a></div>\n<div class="floatright"><div class="noresize" style="height: 252px; width: 350px; "><map name="ImageMap_1_1514097434"><area href="/wiki/Hiiu_County" shape="poly" coords="59,69,91,115,54,130,16,104" alt="Hiiu County" title="Hiiu County" /><area href="/wiki/L%C3%A4%C3%A4ne_County" shape="poly" coords="78,44,134,90,134,126,104,149,80,96" alt="L&#xe4;&#xe4;ne County" title="L&#xe4;&#xe4;ne County" /><area href="/wiki/Saare_County" shape="poly" coords="89,116,107,153,92,232,15,202,8,144" alt="Saare County" title="Saare County" /><area href="/wiki/Harju_County" shape="poly" coords="211,13,225,68,204,69,195,97,167,73,135,95,97,56" alt="Harju County" title="Harju County" /><area href="/wiki/L%C3%A4%C3%A4ne-Viru_County" shape="poly" coords="210,14,225,67,204,70,227,78,225,88,235,97,236,104,264,98,274,76,265,67,264,34" alt="L&#xe4;&#xe4;ne-Viru County" title="L&#xe4;&#xe4;ne-Viru County" /><area href="/wiki/Ida-Viru_County" shape="poly" coords="265,30,264,67,274,76,263,97,279,108,319,97,346,42" alt="Ida-Viru County" title="Ida-Viru County" /><area href="/wiki/Rapla_County" shape="poly" coords="135,95,167,73,194,97,188,124,175,126,171,122,148,128,134,128" alt="Rapla County" title="Rapla County" /><area href="/wiki/P%C3%A4rnu_County" shape="poly" coords="107,149,133,126,148,130,171,122,192,124,189,139,179,143,178,162,192,167,177,196,137,216" alt="P&#xe4;rnu County" title="P&#xe4;rnu County" /><area href="/wiki/J%C3%A4rva_County" shape="poly" coords="189,122,204,69,227,78,225,88,235,96,236,109,216,126,200,135,192,133,194,124" alt="J&#xe4;rva County" title="J&#xe4;rva County" /><area href="/wiki/Viljandi_County" shape="poly" coords="180,145,190,138,191,132,200,134,216,126,236,145,238,190,234,180,222,183,209,201,181,192,193,166,176,159" alt="Viljandi County" title="Viljandi County" /><area href="/wiki/J%C3%B5geva_County" shape="poly" coords="236,145,216,125,236,105,263,97,280,109,291,123,271,136" alt="J&#xf5;geva County" title="J&#xf5;geva County" /><area href="/wiki/Tartu_County" shape="poly" coords="238,145,268,137,296,119,320,175,290,163,262,179,252,174,234,183" alt="Tartu County" title="Tartu County" /><area href="/wiki/Valga_County" shape="poly" coords="208,203,220,183,252,175,262,179,261,196,250,198,258,233,246,237" alt="Valga County" title="Valga County" /><area href="/wiki/P%C3%B5lva_County" shape="poly" coords="260,195,261,179,290,163,319,176,333,204,299,207,298,198" alt="P&#xf5;lva County" title="P&#xf5;lva County" /><area href="/wiki/V%C3%B5ru_County" shape="poly" coords="251,199,261,195,299,199,299,206,323,208,303,242,259,245" alt="V&#xf5;ru County" title="V&#xf5;ru County" /></map><img alt="Counties of Estonia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Eesti_maakonnad_2006_blue.svg/350px-Eesti_maakonnad_2006_blue.svg.png" width="350" height="252" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Eesti_maakonnad_2006_blue.svg/525px-Eesti_maakonnad_2006_blue.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Eesti_maakonnad_2006_blue.svg/700px-Eesti_maakonnad_2006_blue.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="884" data-file-height="636" usemap="#ImageMap_1_1514097434" /><div style="margin-left: 330px; margin-top: -20px; text-align: left;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eesti_maakonnad_2006_blue.svg" title="About this image"><img alt="About this image" src="/w/extensions/ImageMap/desc-20.png?15600" style="border: none;" /></a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Republic of Estonia is divided into fifteen <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Estonia" title="Counties of Estonia">counties</a> <i>(Maakonnad)</i>, which are the administrative subdivisions of the country. The first documented reference to Estonian political and administrative subdivisions comes from the <a href="/wiki/Chronicle_of_Henry_of_Livonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Chronicle of Henry of Livonia">Chronicle of Henry of Livonia</a>, written in the thirteenth century during the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Crusades" title="Northern Crusades">Northern Crusades</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A <i><a href="/wiki/County" title="County">maakond</a></i> (county) is the biggest administrative subdivision. Several changes were made to the borders of counties after Estonia became independent, most notably the formation of <a href="/wiki/Valga_County" title="Valga County">Valga County</a> (from parts of <a href="/wiki/V%C3%B5ru_County" title="V\xc3\xb5ru County">V\xc3\xb5ru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tartu_County" title="Tartu County">Tartu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Viljandi_County" title="Viljandi County">Viljandi</a> counties) and <a href="/wiki/Petseri_County" title="Petseri County">Petseri County</a> (area acquired from Russia with the 1920 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tartu_(Russian%E2%80%93Estonian)" title="Treaty of Tartu (Russian\xe2\x80\x93Estonian)">Tartu Peace Treaty</a>). During the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Estonian SSR">Soviet rule</a>, Petseri County was annexed and ceded to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_SFSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian SFSR">Russian SFSR</a> in 1945 where it became <a href="/wiki/Pechorsky_District" title="Pechorsky District">Pechorsky District</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pskov_Oblast" title="Pskov Oblast">Pskov Oblast</a>. Counties were again re-established on 1 January 1990 in the borders of the Soviet-era <a href="/wiki/Raion" title="Raion">districts</a>. Because of the numerous differences between the current and historical (pre-1940, and sometimes pre-1918) layouts, the historical borders are still used in ethnology, representing cultural and linguistic differences better. Now defunct, the county government <i>(Maavalitsus)</i> of each county used to be led by a county governor <i>(Maavanem)</i>, who represented the national government at the regional level. Governors were appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Estonia" title="Government of Estonia">Government of Estonia</a> for a term of five years.\n</p><p>Each county is further divided into municipalities (<i>omavalitsus</i>), which is also the smallest administrative subdivision of Estonia. There are two types of municipalities: an urban municipality&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 <i>linn</i> (town), and a <a href="/wiki/Rural_municipality" title="Rural municipality">rural municipality</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 <i>vald</i> (parish). There is no other status distinction between them. Each municipality is a unit of <a href="/wiki/Self-government" class="mw-redirect" title="Self-government">self-government</a> with its <a href="/wiki/Representation_(politics)" title="Representation (politics)">representative</a> and executive bodies. The municipalities in Estonia cover the entire territory of the country.\n</p><p>A municipality may contain one or more populated places. <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">Tallinn</a> is divided into eight districts (<i>linnaosa</i>) with limited self-government (<a href="/wiki/Haabersti" title="Haabersti">Haabersti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kesklinn,_Tallinn" title="Kesklinn, Tallinn">Kesklinn</a> (centre), <a href="/wiki/Kristiine" title="Kristiine">Kristiine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lasnam%C3%A4e" title="Lasnam\xc3\xa4e">Lasnam\xc3\xa4e</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mustam%C3%A4e" title="Mustam\xc3\xa4e">Mustam\xc3\xa4e</a>, <a href="/wiki/N%C3%B5mme" title="N\xc3\xb5mme">N\xc3\xb5mme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pirita" title="Pirita">Pirita</a> and <a href="/wiki/P%C3%B5hja-Tallinn" title="P\xc3\xb5hja-Tallinn">P\xc3\xb5hja-Tallinn</a>). Rural municipalities may also be divided into (rural) districts (<i>osavald</i>), most prominent being <a href="/wiki/Hiiumaa_Parish" title="Hiiumaa Parish">Hiiumaa Parish</a> with its five, fairly autonomous districts.\n</p><p>Municipalities range in size of population from Tallinn with around 450,000 inhabitants to <a href="/wiki/Ruhnu" title="Ruhnu">Ruhnu</a> with as few as around 150. They also range fairly in area from Saaremaa Parish (2717,83&#160;km\xc2\xb2) to <a href="/wiki/Loksa" title="Loksa">Loksa</a> town (3,82&#160;km\xc2\xb2). As of October 2017, after the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Administrative_reform_of_Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Administrative reform of Estonia (page does not exist)">Administrative reform of Estonia</a>, there are a total of 79 municipalities in Estonia, 14 of them being urban and 65 rural. Previously there were 213 municipalities.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Estonia" title="Foreign relations of Estonia">Foreign relations of Estonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_missions_of_Estonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Diplomatic missions of Estonia">Diplomatic missions of Estonia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Barack_Obama_giving_a_speech_at_the_Nordea_Concert_Hall_on_2014-09-03_in_Tallinn,_Estonia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/President_Barack_Obama_giving_a_speech_at_the_Nordea_Concert_Hall_on_2014-09-03_in_Tallinn%2C_Estonia.jpg/220px-President_Barack_Obama_giving_a_speech_at_the_Nordea_Concert_Hall_on_2014-09-03_in_Tallinn%2C_Estonia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/President_Barack_Obama_giving_a_speech_at_the_Nordea_Concert_Hall_on_2014-09-03_in_Tallinn%2C_Estonia.jpg/330px-President_Barack_Obama_giving_a_speech_at_the_Nordea_Concert_Hall_on_2014-09-03_in_Tallinn%2C_Estonia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/President_Barack_Obama_giving_a_speech_at_the_Nordea_Concert_Hall_on_2014-09-03_in_Tallinn%2C_Estonia.jpg/440px-President_Barack_Obama_giving_a_speech_at_the_Nordea_Concert_Hall_on_2014-09-03_in_Tallinn%2C_Estonia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Barack_Obama_giving_a_speech_at_the_Nordea_Concert_Hall_on_2014-09-03_in_Tallinn,_Estonia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> giving a speech at the <a href="/wiki/Nordea" title="Nordea">Nordea</a> Concert Hall in <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">Tallinn</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Estonia was a member of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> from 22 September 1921, and became a member of the United Nations on 17 September 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DFAT_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFAT-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> Since restoration of independence Estonia has pursued close relations with the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western countries</a>, and has been member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> since 29 March 2004, as well as the European Union since 1 May 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-DFAT_177-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFAT-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> In 2007 Estonia joined the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, and in 2011 the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DFAT_177-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFAT-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Eu-Lisa" title="Eu-Lisa">European Union Agency for large-scale IT systems</a> is based in Tallinn, which started operations at the end of 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Estonia held the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_the_Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Presidency of the Council of the European Union">Presidency of the Council of the European Union</a> in the second half of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since the early 1990s, Estonia has been involved in active trilateral <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a> co-operation with Latvia and Lithuania, and Nordic-Baltic co-operation with the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic countries</a>. The Baltic Council is the joint forum of the interparliamentary <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Assembly" title="Baltic Assembly">Baltic Assembly</a> and the intergovernmental Baltic Council of Ministers.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Estonia has built close relationship with the Nordic countries, especially <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, and is a member of <a href="/wiki/NB8" class="mw-redirect" title="NB8">Nordic-Baltic Eight <i>(NB-8)</i></a> uniting Nordic and Baltic countries.<sup id="cite_ref-DFAT_177-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFAT-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NB8_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NB8-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> Joint Nordic-Baltic projects include the education programme Nordplus<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> and mobility programmes for business and industry<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> and for public administration.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Council_of_Ministers" class="mw-redirect" title="Nordic Council of Ministers">Nordic Council of Ministers</a> has an office in <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">Tallinn</a> with a subsidiaries in <a href="/wiki/Tartu" title="Tartu">Tartu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Narva" title="Narva">Narva</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The Baltic states are members of <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Investment_Bank" title="Nordic Investment Bank">Nordic Investment Bank</a>, European Union\'s <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Battle_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Nordic Battle Group">Nordic Battle Group</a>, and in 2011 were invited to co-operate with <a href="/wiki/NORDEFCO" title="NORDEFCO">NORDEFCO</a> in selected activities.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Foreign_Ministers_of_Nordic_and_Baltic_countries_met_in_Helsinki,_30.08.2011_(Photographer_Eero_Kuosmanen).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Foreign ministers standing in arc around microphones 2011" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Foreign_Ministers_of_Nordic_and_Baltic_countries_met_in_Helsinki%2C_30.08.2011_%28Photographer_Eero_Kuosmanen%29.jpg/220px-Foreign_Ministers_of_Nordic_and_Baltic_countries_met_in_Helsinki%2C_30.08.2011_%28Photographer_Eero_Kuosmanen%29.jpg"
