srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Foreign_Ministers_of_Nordic_and_Baltic_countries_met_in_Helsinki%2C_30.08.2011_%28Photographer_Eero_Kuosmanen%29.jpg/330px-Foreign_Ministers_of_Nordic_and_Baltic_countries_met_in_Helsinki%2C_30.08.2011_%28Photographer_Eero_Kuosmanen%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Foreign_Ministers_of_Nordic_and_Baltic_countries_met_in_Helsinki%2C_30.08.2011_%28Photographer_Eero_Kuosmanen%29.jpg/440px-Foreign_Ministers_of_Nordic_and_Baltic_countries_met_in_Helsinki%2C_30.08.2011_%28Photographer_Eero_Kuosmanen%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Foreign_Ministers_of_Nordic_and_Baltic_countries_met_in_Helsinki,_30.08.2011_(Photographer_Eero_Kuosmanen).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Foreign ministers of the Nordic and Baltic countries in <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a>, 2011</div></div></div>\n<p>The beginning of the attempt to redefine Estonia as "Nordic" was seen in December 1999, when then Estonian foreign minister (and <a href="/wiki/President_of_Estonia" title="President of Estonia">President of Estonia</a> from 2006 until 2016) <a href="/wiki/Toomas_Hendrik_Ilves" title="Toomas Hendrik Ilves">Toomas Hendrik Ilves</a> delivered a speech entitled "Estonia as a Nordic Country" to the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Institute_for_International_Affairs" title="Swedish Institute for International Affairs">Swedish Institute for International Affairs</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> with potential political calculation behind it being wish to distinguish Estonia from more slowly progressing southern neighbours, which could have postponed early participation in European Union enlargement for Estonia too.<sup id="cite_ref-Mouritzen_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mouritzen-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other Estonian international organization memberships include <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a>, <a href="/wiki/OSCE" class="mw-redirect" title="OSCE">OSCE</a>, <a href="/wiki/WTO" class="mw-redirect" title="WTO">WTO</a>, <a href="/wiki/IMF" class="mw-redirect" title="IMF">IMF</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Baltic_Sea_States" title="Council of the Baltic Sea States">Council of the Baltic Sea States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DFAT_177-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFAT-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> Relations with <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> remain generally cold, although there is some practical cooperation.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Defence_Forces" title="Estonian Defence Forces">Estonian Defence Forces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Defence_League" title="Estonian Defence League">Estonian Defence League</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baltic_Battalion_Soldiers,_Trident_Juncture_15_(22200204329).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Baltic_Battalion_Soldiers%2C_Trident_Juncture_15_%2822200204329%29.jpg/220px-Baltic_Battalion_Soldiers%2C_Trident_Juncture_15_%2822200204329%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Baltic_Battalion_Soldiers%2C_Trident_Juncture_15_%2822200204329%29.jpg/330px-Baltic_Battalion_Soldiers%2C_Trident_Juncture_15_%2822200204329%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Baltic_Battalion_Soldiers%2C_Trident_Juncture_15_%2822200204329%29.jpg/440px-Baltic_Battalion_Soldiers%2C_Trident_Juncture_15_%2822200204329%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baltic_Battalion_Soldiers,_Trident_Juncture_15_(22200204329).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Estonian soldiers during a NATO exercise in 2015</div></div></div>\n<p>The military of Estonia is based upon the Estonian Defence Forces (<a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a>: <i lang="et">Kaitsev\xc3\xa4gi</i>), which is the name of the unified armed forces of the republic with <i><a href="/wiki/Maav%C3%A4gi" class="mw-redirect" title="Maav\xc3\xa4gi">Maav\xc3\xa4gi</a></i> (Army), <i><a href="/wiki/Estonian_Navy" title="Estonian Navy">Merev\xc3\xa4gi</a></i> (Navy), <i><a href="/wiki/Estonian_Air_Force" title="Estonian Air Force">\xc3\x95huv\xc3\xa4gi</a></i> (Air Force) and a paramilitary national guard organisation <i><a href="/wiki/Estonian_Defence_League" title="Estonian Defence League">Kaitseliit</a></i> (Defence League). The Estonian National Defence Policy aim is to guarantee the preservation of the independence and <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> of the state, the <a href="/wiki/Integrity" title="Integrity">integrity</a> of its land, territorial waters, airspace and its constitutional order.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Current strategic goals are to defend the country\'s interests, develop the armed forces for <a href="/wiki/Interoperability" title="Interoperability">interoperability</a> with other <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and EU member forces, and participation in NATO missions.\n</p><p>The current national <a href="/wiki/Military_service" title="Military service">military service</a> (<a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a>: <i lang="et">ajateenistus</i>) is compulsory for men between 18 and 28, and conscripts serve eight-month to eleven-month tours of duty depending on the army branch they serve in. Estonia has retained <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a> unlike Latvia and Lithuania and has no plan to transition to a <a href="/wiki/Standing_army" title="Standing army">professional army</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, annual military spending reached 1.85% of GDP, or 5&#160;billion <a href="/wiki/Estonian_kroon" title="Estonian kroon">kroons</a>, and was expected to continue to increase until 2010, when a 2.0% level was anticipated.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Estonia co-operates with Latvia and Lithuania in several trilateral Baltic defence co-operation initiatives, including Baltic Battalion (BALTBAT), Baltic Naval Squadron (BALTRON), Baltic Air Surveillance Network (BALTNET) and joint military educational institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Defence_College" title="Baltic Defence College">Baltic Defence College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tartu" title="Tartu">Tartu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> Future co-operation will include sharing of national infrastructures for training purposes and specialisation of training areas (BALTTRAIN) and collective formation of battalion-sized contingents for use in the NATO rapid-response force.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> In January 2011 the Baltic states were invited to join <a href="/wiki/NORDEFCO" title="NORDEFCO">NORDEFCO</a>, the defence framework of the Nordic countries.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:XA-180EST_in_Afghanistan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Estonian armoured car in desert camouflage Afghanistan" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/XA-180EST_in_Afghanistan.jpg/220px-XA-180EST_in_Afghanistan.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/XA-180EST_in_Afghanistan.jpg/330px-XA-180EST_in_Afghanistan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/XA-180EST_in_Afghanistan.jpg/440px-XA-180EST_in_Afghanistan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:XA-180EST_in_Afghanistan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Estonian <a href="/wiki/Patria_Pasi" title="Patria Pasi">Patria Pasi</a> XA-180 in Afghanistan</div></div></div>\n<p>In January 2008, the Estonian military had almost 300 troops stationed in foreign countries as part of various international peacekeeping forces, including 35 Defence League troops stationed in Kosovo; 120 <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Estonian Army">Ground Forces</a> soldiers in the NATO-led <a href="/wiki/International_Security_Assistance_Force" title="International Security Assistance Force">ISAF</a> force in Afghanistan; 80 soldiers stationed as a part of MNF in Iraq; and 2 Estonian officers in Bosnia-Herzegovina and 2 Estonian military agents in Israeli occupied <a href="/wiki/Golan_Heights" title="Golan Heights">Golan Heights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Estonian Defence Forces have also previously had military missions in Croatia from March until October 1995, in Lebanon from December 1996 until June 1997 and in Macedonia from May until December 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> Estonia participates in the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Battlegroup" title="Nordic Battlegroup">Nordic Battlegroup</a> and has announced readiness to send soldiers also to Sudan to <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur</a> if necessary, creating the first African <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> mission for the armed forces of Estonia.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Ministry_of_Defence" class="mw-redirect" title="Estonian Ministry of Defence">Ministry of Defence</a> and the Defence Forces have been working on a <a href="/wiki/Cyberwarfare" title="Cyberwarfare">cyberwarfare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Defense_(military)" class="mw-redirect" title="Defense (military)">defence</a> <a href="/wiki/Formation_(military)" class="mw-redirect" title="Formation (military)">formation</a> for some years now. In 2007, a <a href="/wiki/Military_doctrine" title="Military doctrine">military doctrine</a> of an <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Estonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Estonia">e-military of Estonia</a> was officially introduced as the country was under <a href="/wiki/2007_cyberattacks_on_Estonia" title="2007 cyberattacks on Estonia">massive cyberattacks in 2007</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_gal_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_gal-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> The proposed aim of the e-military is to secure the vital infrastructure and <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">e-infrastructure</a> of Estonia. The main cyber warfare facility is the Computer Emergency Response Team of Estonia (CERT), founded in 2006. The organisation operates on security issues in local networks.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Then President of the US, <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>, announced his support of Estonia as the location of a NATO <a href="/wiki/Cooperative_Cyber_Defence_Centre_of_Excellence" title="Cooperative Cyber Defence Centre of Excellence">Cooperative Cyber Defence Centre of Excellence</a> (CCDCOE) in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> In the aftermath of the 2007 cyberattacks, plans to combine network defence with Estonian military doctrine have been nicknamed as the Tiger\'s Defence, in reference to Tiigrih\xc3\xbcpe.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> The CCDCOE started its operations in November 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Estonia" title="Economy of Estonia">Economy of Estonia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone.svg" class="image"><img alt="map of European Union eurozone" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/220px-BlueEurozone.svg.png" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/330px-BlueEurozone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/440px-BlueEurozone.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="645" data-file-height="690" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Estonia is part of a monetary union, the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> (dark blue), and of the <a href="/wiki/Internal_Market_(European_Union)" class="mw-redirect" title="Internal Market (European Union)">EU single market</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tln1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="aerial view of high rises at sunset" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Tln1.jpg/220px-Tln1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Tln1.jpg/330px-Tln1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Tln1.jpg/440px-Tln1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5473" data-file-height="3655" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tln1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The central business district of <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">Tallinn</a></div></div></div>\n<p>As a member of the European Union, Estonia is considered a high-income economy by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">GDP (PPP) per capita</a> of the country was $29,312 in 2016 according to the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-imf2_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf2-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Because of its rapid growth, Estonia has often been described as a <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Tiger" title="Baltic Tiger">Baltic Tiger</a> beside Lithuania and Latvia. Beginning 1 January 2011, Estonia adopted the euro and became the 17th <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> member state.<sup id="cite_ref-euroreuters_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euroreuters-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>, Estonia had the lowest ratio of government debt to GDP among EU countries at 6.7% at the end of 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Skype_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="logo of skype white letters on blue background" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Skype_logo.svg/220px-Skype_logo.svg.png" width="220" height="98" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Skype_logo.svg/330px-Skype_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Skype_logo.svg/440px-Skype_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="208" data-file-height="93" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Skype_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The IT sector\'s share in GDP has sharply increased since 2004. <a href="/wiki/Skype" title="Skype">Skype</a> was created by Estonian developers and is mainly developed in Estonia.</div></div></div>\n<p>A balanced budget, almost non-existent <a href="/wiki/Public_debt" class="mw-redirect" title="Public debt">public debt</a>, flat-rate income tax, free trade regime, competitive commercial banking sector, innovative <a href="/wiki/E-Services" class="mw-redirect" title="E-Services">e-Services</a> and even mobile-based services are all hallmarks of Estonia\'s market economy.\n</p><p>Estonia produces about 75% of its consumed electricity.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, about 85% of it was generated with locally mined <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale" title="Oil shale">oil shale</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> Alternative energy sources such as wood, peat, and biomass make up approximately 9% of primary energy production. Renewable wind energy was about 6% of total consumption in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> Estonia imports <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a> products from western Europe and Russia. Estonia imports 100% of its <a href="/wiki/Russia_in_the_European_energy_sector" title="Russia in the European energy sector">natural gas from Russia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> Oil shale energy, telecommunications, textiles, chemical products, banking, services, food and fishing, timber, shipbuilding, electronics, and transportation are key sectors of the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ice-free_port" class="mw-redirect" title="Ice-free port">ice-free port</a> of <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Muuga" class="mw-redirect" title="Port of Muuga">Muuga</a>, near Tallinn, is a modern facility featuring good transshipment capability, a high-capacity grain elevator, chill/frozen storage, and new oil tanker off-loading capabilities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The railroad serves as a conduit between the West, Russia, and other points to the East.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Because of the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932010" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x932010">global economic recession that began in 2007</a>, the GDP of Estonia decreased by 1.4% in the 2nd quarter of 2008, over 3% in the 3rd quarter of 2008, and over 9% in the 4th quarter of 2008. The Estonian government made a supplementary negative budget, which was passed by <a href="/wiki/Riigikogu" title="Riigikogu">Riigikogu</a>. The revenue of the budget was decreased for 2008 by EEK 6.1&#160;billion and the expenditure by EEK 3.2&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, the economic situation stabilised and started a growth based on strong exports. In the fourth quarter of 2010, Estonian industrial output increased by 23% compared to the year before. The country has been experiencing economic growth ever since.<sup id="cite_ref-Stat_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stat-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to Eurostat data, Estonian PPS GDP per capita stood at 67% of the EU average in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, the average monthly gross salary in Estonia was \xe2\x82\xac1221.<sup id="cite_ref-StatisticsEstonia_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StatisticsEstonia-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>However, there are vast disparities in GDP between different areas of Estonia; currently, over half of the country\'s GDP is created in Tallinn.<sup id="cite_ref-BBN_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBN-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, the GDP per capita of Tallinn stood at 172% of the Estonian average,<sup id="cite_ref-Statistics_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statistics-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> which makes the per capita GDP of Tallinn as high as 115% of the European Union average, exceeding the average levels of other counties.\n</p><p>The unemployment rate in March 2016 was 6.4%, which is below the EU average,<sup id="cite_ref-StatisticsEstonia_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StatisticsEstonia-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> while real GDP growth in 2011 was 8.0%,<sup id="cite_ref-Statistics_Estonia_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statistics_Estonia-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> five times the euro-zone average. In 2012, Estonia remained the only euro member with a budget surplus, and with a national debt of only 6%, it is one of the least indebted countries in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_indicators">Economic indicators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Economic indicators">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Estonia\'s economy continues to benefit from a transparent government and policies that sustain a high level of <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">economic freedom</a>, ranking 6th globally and 2nd in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> The rule of <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Estonia" title="Law of Estonia">law</a> remains strongly buttressed and enforced by an independent and efficient judicial system. A simplified tax system with flat rates and low indirect taxation, openness to foreign investment, and a liberal trade regime have supported the resilient and well-functioning economy.<sup id="cite_ref-taxfoundation1_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taxfoundation1-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> The 2017 <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_Doing_Business_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Ease of Doing Business Index">Ease of Doing Business Index</a> by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank Group</a> places the country 12th in the world, surpassing neighbouring Finland, Australia, Germany, Canada and Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> The strong focus on the IT sector has led to much faster, simpler and efficient public services where for example filing a tax return takes less than five minutes and 98% of banking transactions are conducted through the internet.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> Estonia has the third lowest business bribery risk in the world, according to TRACE Matrix.<sup id="cite_ref-traceinternational.org_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-traceinternational.org-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="BarChartTemplate" style="border-style:solid; background:#7CB9E8; color:white;">76.5\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_development">Historic development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Historic development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1928, a stable currency, the <i><a href="/wiki/Estonian_kroon" title="Estonian kroon">kroon</a></i>, was established. It is issued by the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Estonia" title="Bank of Estonia">Bank of Estonia</a>, the country\'s <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a>. The word <i>kroon</i> (<small>Estonian pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Estonian_and_Finnish" title="Help:IPA/Estonian and Finnish">[\xcb\x88kro\xcb\x90n]</a></span>, "crown") is related to that of the other <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic</a> currencies (such as the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_krona" title="Swedish krona">Swedish krona</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Danish_krone" title="Danish krone">Danish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_krone" title="Norwegian krone">Norwegian krone</a>). The kroon succeeded the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_mark" title="Estonian mark">mark</a> in 1928 and was used until 1940. After Estonia regained its independence, the kroon was reintroduced in 1992.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Real_GDP_growth_in_Estonia,_2002-2012.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Real_GDP_growth_in_Estonia%2C_2002-2012.png/220px-Real_GDP_growth_in_Estonia%2C_2002-2012.png" width="220" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Real_GDP_growth_in_Estonia%2C_2002-2012.png/330px-Real_GDP_growth_in_Estonia%2C_2002-2012.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Real_GDP_growth_in_Estonia%2C_2002-2012.png/440px-Real_GDP_growth_in_Estonia%2C_2002-2012.png 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="354" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Real_GDP_growth_in_Estonia,_2002-2012.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Estonia\'s GDP growth from 2000 till 2012</div></div></div>\n<p>Since <a href="/wiki/History_of_Estonia#Regaining_independence" title="History of Estonia">re-establishing independence</a>, Estonia has styled itself as the gateway between East and West and aggressively pursued economic reform and integration with the West. Estonia\'s market reforms put it among the economic leaders in the former <a href="/wiki/COMECON" class="mw-redirect" title="COMECON">COMECON</a> area.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In 1994, based on the economic theories of <a href="/wiki/Milton_Friedman" title="Milton Friedman">Milton Friedman</a>, Estonia became one of the first countries to adopt a <a href="/wiki/Flat_tax" title="Flat tax">flat tax</a>, with a uniform rate of 26% regardless of personal income. This rate has since been reduced three times, to 24% in January 2005, 23% in January 2006, and finally to 21% by January 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Estonia" title="Government of Estonia">Government of Estonia</a> finalised the design of <a href="/wiki/Estonian_euro_coins" title="Estonian euro coins">Estonian euro coins</a> in late 2004, and adopted the euro as the country\'s currency on 1 January 2011, later than planned due to continued high inflation.<sup id="cite_ref-euroreuters_210-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euroreuters-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-euro-EFP_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euro-EFP-234">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Land_Value_Tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Land Value Tax">Land Value Tax</a> is levied which is used to fund local municipalities. It is a state level tax, however 100% of the revenue is used to fund Local Councils. The rate is set by the Local Council within the limits of 0.1\xe2\x80\x932.5%. It is one of the most important sources of funding for municipalities.<sup id="cite_ref-Land_Tax_Reform_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Land_Tax_Reform-235">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> The Land Value Tax is levied on the value of the land only with improvements and buildings not considered. Very few exemptions are considered on the land value tax and even public institutions are subject to the tax.<sup id="cite_ref-Land_Tax_Reform_235-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Land_Tax_Reform-235">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> The tax has contributed to a high rate (~90%)<sup id="cite_ref-Land_Tax_Reform_235-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Land_Tax_Reform-235">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> of owner-occupied residences within Estonia, compared to a rate of 67.4% in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1999, Estonia experienced its worst year economically since it regained independence in 1991, largely because of the impact of the <a href="/wiki/1998_Russian_financial_crisis" title="1998 Russian financial crisis">1998 Russian financial crisis</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Estonia joined the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a> in November 1999. With assistance from the European Union, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Investment_Bank" title="Nordic Investment Bank">Nordic Investment Bank</a>, Estonia completed most of its preparations for European Union membership by the end of 2002 and now has one of the strongest economies of the new member states of the European Union.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Estonia joined the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a> in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Resources">Resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Estonian_shale.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Estonian_shale.JPG/220px-Estonian_shale.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Estonian_shale.JPG/330px-Estonian_shale.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Estonian_shale.JPG/440px-Estonian_shale.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4912" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Estonian_shale.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale_in_Estonia" title="Oil shale in Estonia">oil shale industry</a> in Estonia is one of the most developed in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-iea_20_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iea_20-238">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, oil shale supplied 70% of Estonia\'s <a href="/wiki/Total_primary_energy_supply" class="mw-redirect" title="Total primary energy supply">total primary energy</a> and accounted for 4% of Estonia\'s gross domestic product.<sup id="cite_ref-audit_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-audit-239">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-iea_7_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iea_7-240">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Although Estonia is in general resource-poor, the land still offers a large variety of smaller resources. The country has large <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale" title="Oil shale">oil shale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> deposits, along with forests that cover 48% of the land.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> In addition to oil shale and limestone, Estonia also has large reserves of <a href="/wiki/Phosphorite" title="Phosphorite">phosphorite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uraninite" title="Uraninite">pitchblende</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> that currently are not mined, or not mined extensively.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Significant quantities of <a href="/wiki/Rare-earth" class="mw-redirect" title="Rare-earth">rare-earth</a> oxides are found in tailings accumulated from 50 years of <a href="/wiki/Uranium_ore" title="Uranium ore">uranium ore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shale" title="Shale">shale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Loparite" class="mw-redirect" title="Loparite">loparite</a> mining at <a href="/wiki/Sillam%C3%A4e" title="Sillam\xc3\xa4e">Sillam\xc3\xa4e</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> Because of the rising prices of rare earths, extraction of these oxides has become economically viable. The country currently exports around 3000 tonnes per annum, representing around 2% of world production.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 2008, public debate has discussed whether Estonia should build a nuclear power plant to secure energy production after closure of old units in the <a href="/wiki/Narva_Power_Plants" title="Narva Power Plants">Narva Power Plants</a>, if they are not reconstructed by the year 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry_and_environment">Industry and environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Industry and environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale_in_Estonia" title="Oil shale in Estonia">Oil shale in Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Narva_Power_Plants" title="Narva Power Plants">Narva Power Plants</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_Estonia" title="Wind power in Estonia">Wind power in Estonia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hanila_tuulepark_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="R\xc3\xb5uste wind turbines next to wetland" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Hanila_tuulepark_2.JPG/220px-Hanila_tuulepark_2.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Hanila_tuulepark_2.JPG/330px-Hanila_tuulepark_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Hanila_tuulepark_2.JPG/440px-Hanila_tuulepark_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hanila_tuulepark_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>R\xc3\xb5uste wind farm in <a href="/wiki/Hanila_Parish" title="Hanila Parish">Hanila Parish</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Food, construction, and electronic industries are currently among the most important branches of Estonia\'s industry.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In 2007, the construction industry employed more than 80,000 people, around 12% of the entire country\'s workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> Another important industrial sector is the machinery and chemical industry, which is mainly located in <a href="/wiki/Ida-Viru_County" title="Ida-Viru County">Ida-Viru County</a> and around Tallinn.\n</p><p>The oil shale-based <a href="/wiki/Mining_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Mining industry">mining industry</a>, which is also concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Virumaa" title="Virumaa">East-Estonia</a>, produces around 90% of the entire country\'s electricity.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Although the amount of pollutants emitted to the air have been falling since the 1980s,<sup id="cite_ref-Auer_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auer-248">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> the air is still polluted with <a href="/wiki/Sulphur_dioxide" class="mw-redirect" title="Sulphur dioxide">sulphur dioxide</a> from the mining industry that the Soviet Union rapidly developed in the early 1950s. In some areas the coastal seawater is polluted, mainly around the <a href="/wiki/Sillam%C3%A4e" title="Sillam\xc3\xa4e">Sillam\xc3\xa4e</a> industrial complex.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Estonia is a dependent country in the terms of energy and energy production. In recent years many local and foreign companies have been investing in renewable energy sources.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The importance of wind power has been increasing steadily in Estonia and currently the total amount of energy production from wind is nearly 60 <a href="/wiki/Megawatt" class="mw-redirect" title="Megawatt">MW</a> while at the same time roughly 399&#160;MW worth of projects are currently being developed and more than 2800&#160;MW worth of projects are being proposed in the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Peipus" title="Lake Peipus">Lake Peipus</a> area and the coastal areas of <a href="/wiki/Hiiumaa" title="Hiiumaa">Hiiumaa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Currently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (February 2011)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>, there are plans to renovate some older units of the Narva Power Plants, establish new power stations, and provide higher efficiency in oil shale-based energy production.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> Estonia liberalised 35% of its electricity market in April 2010. The electricity market as whole will be liberalised by 2013.\n<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Together with Lithuania, Poland, and Latvia, the country considered participating in constructing the <a href="/wiki/Visaginas_nuclear_power_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Visaginas nuclear power plant">Visaginas nuclear power plant</a> in Lithuania to replace the <a href="/wiki/Ignalina_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Ignalina Nuclear Power Plant">Ignalina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wnn-lt_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wnn-lt-255">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-le_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-le-256">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> However, due to the slow pace of the project and problems with the sector (like <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daiichi_nuclear_disaster" title="Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster">Fukushima disaster</a> and bad example of <a href="/wiki/Olkiluoto_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Olkiluoto Nuclear Power Plant">Olkiluoto plant</a>), <a href="/wiki/Eesti_Energia" title="Eesti Energia">Eesti Energia</a> has shifted its main focus to <a href="/wiki/Shale_oil" title="Shale oil">shale oil</a> production that is seen as much more profitable business.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Estonia has a strong information technology <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Quaternary sector of the economy">sector</a>, partly owing to the <a href="/wiki/Tiigrih%C3%BCpe" title="Tiigrih\xc3\xbcpe">Tiigrih\xc3\xbcpe</a> project undertaken in the mid-1990s, and has been mentioned as the most "wired" and advanced country in Europe in the terms of e-Government of Estonia.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> A new direction is to offer those services present in Estonia to the non-residents via <a href="/wiki/E-residency_of_Estonia" class="mw-redirect" title="E-residency of Estonia">e-residency program</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Skype" title="Skype">Skype</a> was written by Estonia-based developers <a href="/wiki/Ahti_Heinla" title="Ahti Heinla">Ahti Heinla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Priit_Kasesalu" title="Priit Kasesalu">Priit Kasesalu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jaan_Tallinn" title="Jaan Tallinn">Jaan Tallinn</a>, who had also originally developed <a href="/wiki/Kazaa" title="Kazaa">Kazaa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> Other notable tech startups include <a href="/wiki/GrabCAD" title="GrabCAD">GrabCAD</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fortumo" title="Fortumo">Fortumo</a> and <a href="/wiki/TransferWise" title="TransferWise">TransferWise</a>. It is even claimed that Estonia has the most startups per person in world.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Estonian electricity network forms a part of the <a href="/wiki/Nord_Pool_Spot" class="mw-redirect" title="Nord Pool Spot">Nord Pool Spot</a> network.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trade">Trade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Trade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote style="text-align:right">-%</td>\n<td style="text-align:right">3%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Estonia has had a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a> since the end of the 1990s and one of the highest per capita income levels in Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> Proximity to the Scandinavian and Finnish markets, its location between the East and West, competitive cost structure and a highly skilled labour force have been the major Estonian comparative advantages in the beginning of the 2000s (decade). As the largest city, Tallinn has emerged as a <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial centre</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tallinn_Stock_Exchange" title="Tallinn Stock Exchange">Tallinn Stock Exchange</a> joined recently with the <a href="/wiki/OMX" class="mw-redirect" title="OMX">OMX</a> system. Several cryptocurrency trading platforms are officially recognized by the government, such as <a href="/w/index.php?title=CoinMetro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="CoinMetro (page does not exist)">CoinMetro</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> The current government has pursued tight <a href="/wiki/Finance" title="Finance">fiscal</a> policies, resulting in balanced budgets and low <a href="/wiki/Public_debt" class="mw-redirect" title="Public debt">public debt</a>.\n</p><p>In 2007, however, a large current account deficit and rising inflation put pressure on <a href="/wiki/Estonian_kroon" title="Estonian kroon">Estonia\'s currency</a>, which was pegged to the Euro, highlighting the need for growth in export-generating industries.\nEstonia exports mainly machinery and equipment, wood and paper, textiles, food products, furniture, and metals and chemical products.<sup id="cite_ref-CIAworld_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIAworld-265">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> Estonia also exports 1.562&#160;billion kilowatt hours of electricity annually.<sup id="cite_ref-CIAworld_265-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIAworld-265">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> At the same time Estonia imports machinery and equipment, chemical products, textiles, food products and transportation equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-CIAworld_265-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIAworld-265">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> Estonia imports 200&#160;million kilowatt hours of electricity annually.<sup id="cite_ref-CIAworld_265-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIAworld-265">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Between 2007 and 2013, Estonia received 53.3&#160;billion <a href="/wiki/Estonian_kroon" title="Estonian kroon">kroons</a> (3.4&#160;billion euros) from various European Union Structural Funds as direct supports, creating the largest foreign investments into Estonia.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> Majority of the European Union financial aid will be invested into the following fields: energy economies, entrepreneurship, administrative capability, education, information society, environment protection, regional and local development, research and development activities, healthcare and welfare, transportation and labour market.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> Main sources of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investments</a> to Estonia are Sweden and Finland (As of 31 December 2016 48.3%).<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Eesti_rahvaarv_1970-2009.png/420px-Eesti_rahvaarv_1970-2009.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Eesti_rahvaarv_1970-2009.png/560px-Eesti_rahvaarv_1970-2009.png 2x" data-file-width="571" data-file-height="334" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eesti_rahvaarv_1970-2009.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population of Estonia 1970\xe2\x80\x932009. The changes are largely attributed to Soviet immigration and emigration.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Before World War II, ethnic <a href="/wiki/Estonians" title="Estonians">Estonians</a> constituted 88% of the population, with national minorities constituting the remaining 12%.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnic_minor_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnic_minor-270">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> The largest minority groups in 1934 were <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swedish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Swedish people">Swedes</a>, Latvians, <a href="/wiki/Jewish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish people">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finns" title="Finns">Finns</a> and <a href="/wiki/Izhorians" title="Izhorians">Ingrians</a>.\n</p><p>The share of <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Germans" title="Baltic Germans">Baltic Germans</a> in Estonia had fallen from 5.3% (~46,700) in 1881 to 1.3% (16,346) by the year 1934,<sup id="cite_ref-ethnic_minor_270-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnic_minor-270">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-baltic_germans_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baltic_germans-271">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> which was mainly due to emigration to Germany in the light of general Russification in the end of the 19th century and the independence of Estonia in the 20th century.\n</p><p>Between 1945 and 1989, the share of ethnic Estonians in the population resident within the currently defined boundaries of Estonia dropped to 61%, caused primarily by the Soviet programme promoting mass immigration of urban industrial workers from Russia, Ukraine, and Belarus, as well as by wartime emigration and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>\'s mass deportations and executions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> By 1989, minorities constituted more than one-third of the population, as the number of non-Estonians had grown almost fivefold.\n</p><p>At the end of the 1980s, Estonians perceived their demographic change as a <a href="/wiki/Disaster" title="Disaster">national catastrophe</a>. This was a result of the <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">migration</a> policies essential to the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Estonian SSR">Soviet Nationalisation Programme</a> aiming to <a href="/wiki/Russify" class="mw-redirect" title="Russify">russify</a> Estonia \xe2\x80\x93 administrative and military immigration of non-Estonians from the USSR coupled with the deportation of Estonians to the USSR. In the decade after the reconstitution of independence, large-scale emigration by ethnic Russians and the removal of the Russian military bases in 1994 caused the proportion of ethnic Estonians in Estonia to increase from 61% to 69% in 2006.\n</p><p>Modern Estonia is a fairly ethnically heterogeneous country, but this heterogeneity is not a feature of much of the country as the non-Estonian population is concentrated in two of Estonia\'s counties. Thirteen of Estonia\'s 15 counties are over 80% ethnic Estonian, the most homogeneous being <a href="/wiki/Hiiumaa" title="Hiiumaa">Hiiumaa</a>, where Estonians account for 98.4% of the population. In the counties of <a href="/wiki/Harju_County" title="Harju County">Harju</a> (including the capital city, <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">Tallinn</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Ida-Viru_County" title="Ida-Viru County">Ida-Viru</a>, however, ethnic Estonians make up 60% and 20% of the population, respectively. <a href="/wiki/History_of_Russians_in_Estonia" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Russians in Estonia">Russians</a> make up 25.6% of the total population but account for 36% of the population in Harju county and 70% of the population in Ida-Viru county.\n</p><p>The Estonian Cultural Autonomy law that was passed in 1925 was unique in Europe at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> Cultural autonomies could be granted to <a href="/wiki/Minorities" class="mw-redirect" title="Minorities">minorities</a> numbering more than 3,000 people with longstanding ties to the Republic of Estonia. Before the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Estonian SSR">Soviet occupation</a>, the Germans and Jewish minorities managed to elect a cultural council. The Law on Cultural Autonomy for National Minorities was reinstated in 1993. Historically, large parts of Estonia\'s northwestern coast and islands have been populated by indigenous ethnically <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Swedes" title="Estonian Swedes">Rannarootslased</a> (Coastal Swedes).\n</p><p>In recent years the numbers of Coastal Swedes has risen again, numbering in 2008 almost 500 people, owing to the property reforms in the beginning of the 1990s. In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Ingrian_Finnish" class="mw-redirect" title="Ingrian Finnish">Ingrian Finnish</a> minority in Estonia elected a cultural council and was granted cultural autonomy. The <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Swedes" title="Estonian Swedes">Estonian Swedish</a> minority similarly received cultural autonomy in 2007.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Estonia" title="Human rights in Estonia">Human rights in Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nordic_identity_in_Estonia" title="Nordic identity in Estonia">Nordic identity in Estonia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Estonian_alien%27s_passport" title="Estonian alien&#39;s passport">Estonian alien\'s passport</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Viljandi_folkdanslag_p%C3%A5_Hedemora_gammelg%C3%A5rd_2014_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Viljandi_folkdanslag_p%C3%A5_Hedemora_gammelg%C3%A5rd_2014_01.jpg/220px-Viljandi_folkdanslag_p%C3%A5_Hedemora_gammelg%C3%A5rd_2014_01.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Viljandi_folkdanslag_p%C3%A5_Hedemora_gammelg%C3%A5rd_2014_01.jpg/330px-Viljandi_folkdanslag_p%C3%A5_Hedemora_gammelg%C3%A5rd_2014_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Viljandi_folkdanslag_p%C3%A5_Hedemora_gammelg%C3%A5rd_2014_01.jpg/440px-Viljandi_folkdanslag_p%C3%A5_Hedemora_gammelg%C3%A5rd_2014_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1515" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Viljandi_folkdanslag_p%C3%A5_Hedemora_gammelg%C3%A5rd_2014_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Viljandi" title="Viljandi">Viljandi</a> folk dance group performing at <a href="/wiki/Hedemora_gammelg%C3%A5rd" title="Hedemora gammelg\xc3\xa5rd">Hedemora gammelg\xc3\xa5rd</a>, Sweden.</div></div></div>\n<p>Estonian society has undergone considerable changes over the last twenty years, one of the most notable being the increasing level of stratification, and the distribution of family income. The <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini coefficient</a> has been steadily higher than the European Union average (31 in 2009),<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> although it has clearly dropped. The registered unemployment rate in January 2012 was 7.7%.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Modern Estonia is a multinational country in which 109 languages are spoken, according to a 2000 census. 67.3% of Estonian citizens speak <a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a> as their native language, 29.7% Russian, and 3% speak other languages.<sup id="cite_ref-PopulationByNationality_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopulationByNationality-275">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> As of 2 July 2010, 84.1% of Estonian residents are Estonian citizens, 8.6% are citizens of other countries and 7.3% are "citizens with undetermined citizenship".<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> Since 1992 roughly 140,000 people have acquired Estonian citizenship by passing <a href="/wiki/Naturalisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Naturalisation">naturalisation</a> exams.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> Estonia has also accepted <a href="/wiki/European_migrant_crisis#Relocation_and_resettlement_of_asylum_seekers" title="European migrant crisis">quota refugees</a> under the migrant plan agreed upon by EU member states in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The ethnic distribution in Estonia is very homogeneous, where in most counties over 90% of the people are ethnic <a href="/wiki/Estonians" title="Estonians">Estonians</a>. This is in contrast to large urban centres like <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">Tallinn</a>, where Estonians account for 60% of the population, and the remainder is composed mostly of Russian and other Slavic inhabitants, who arrived in Estonia during the Soviet period.\n</p><p>The 2008 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">United Nations Human Rights Council</a> report called "extremely credible" the description of the <a href="/wiki/Estonian_nationality_law" title="Estonian nationality law">citizenship policy of Estonia</a> as "discriminatory".<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> According to surveys, only 5% of the Russian community have considered returning to Russia in the near future. Estonian Russians have developed their own identity \xe2\x80\x93 more than half of the respondents recognised that Estonian Russians differ noticeably from the Russians in Russia. When comparing the result with a survey from 2000, then Russians\' attitude toward the future is much more positive.<sup id="cite_ref-Societal_survey_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Societal_survey-280">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Estonia has been the first post-Soviet republic that has legalised civil unions of same-sex couples. The law was approved in October 2014 and came into effect 1 January 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>53.3% of ethnically Estonian youth consider belonging in the Nordic identity group as important or very important for them. 52.2% have the same attitude towards the "Baltic" identity group, according to a research study from 2013 <sup id="cite_ref-inimareng.ee_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inimareng.ee-282">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The image that Estonian youths have of their identity is rather similar to that of the Finns as far as the identities of being a citizen of one\xe2\x80\x99s own country, a Fenno-Ugric person, or a Nordic person are concerned, while our identity as a citizen of Europe is common ground between us and Latvians - being stronger here than it is among the young people of Finland and Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-inimareng.ee_282-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inimareng.ee-282">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanization">Urbanization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Estonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Urbanization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Estonia" title="List of cities and towns in Estonia">List of cities and towns in Estonia</a></div>\n<p>Tallinn is the capital and the largest city of Estonia. It lies on the northern coast of Estonia, along the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Finland" title="Gulf of Finland">Gulf of Finland</a>. There are 33 cities and several town-parish towns in the country. In total, there are 47 <i>linn</i>a, with "linn" in English meaning both "cities" and "towns". More than 70% of the population lives in towns. The 20 largest cities are listed below:\n</p>\n<table class="navbox">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="10" class="navbox-title"><div style="float:right; width:6em; height:2.6em">&#160;</div><div style="text-align:right;">12,167\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">3</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Narva" title="Narva">Narva</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">5,485\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">10</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Sillam%C3%A4e" style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">20</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Tapa,_Estonia" title="Tapa, Estonia">Tapa</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Estonia" title="Religion in Estonia">Religion in Estonia</a></div>\n<div style="float:right; margin:0; margin-left:7px;">\n<table
